Lineage of Child from Revocable Divorce After Two Years
Ruling on lineage when a divorced woman gives birth after more than two years

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school establishes lineage for a child born more than two years after a revocable divorce, and identify the condition under which lineage is not established.

Core Idea
Lineage is established unless the woman admits her iddah ended, because iddah may be prolonged by extended purity.

A common assumption is that a child born more than two years after divorce cannot be attributed to the former husband. This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies the Hanafi position: as long as the woman has not admitted the end of her iddah, the possibility of intercourse during the iddah and the possibility of extended purity (mumtaddat al-tuhr) keep the lineage intact. Let us examine the ruling, its proofs, and the one exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويثبت نسب ولد معتدةِ الرّجعي، وإن جاءَت به لأكثر من سنتين ما لم تقر بانقضاء العدة) ؛ لاحتمال العلوق في العدة، وجواز كون المرأة ممتدة الطهر، أما لو أقرت بانقضاء العدة ، ثم ولدت ، وبين الطلاق والولادة أكثر من سنتين لا يثبت النسب
قوله : على أنّ... الخ ؛ علاوة على ما ذكر، وحاصلها تأييد ثبوت النسب بأنّ الزوج إن كان يعلم بعدم العلوق بعد الفراش الصحيح، بأن لم يكن يطأها في تلك الليلة المعينة، أو كان وطئها وعَلِمَ تقدّم العلوق على النكاح ، كان يلزم عليه أن يلاعن معها، وينفي ولدها من نفسه، فلما سكت عنه، وإمكانُ العلوق في حال الفراش ممكن بأحد الصور المذكورة ، لَزِمَ علينا الاحتياط في إثباته.
قوله : لأكثر ؛ أي ولدت بعد الطلاق لأكثر من سنتين، ولو بعشرين سنة.
قوله : لاحتمال ... الخ ؛ حاصله : أنه يحتمل أن يكون الوطء في العدة ؛ لأنَّ عدة الرجعي لا تحرم الوطء، وتكون المرأة ممتدة ،الطهر، بأن يكون الفاصل بين حيضتها زماناً كثيراً ؛ إذ لا مدة لأكثر الطهر ، فتكون العدّة لم تنقض في سنتين، بل في أكثر منهما أيضاً ؛ لعدم وجود ثلاث حيض، بسبب امتداد الطهر.
قوله : بانقضاء العدة ؛ والمدة تحتمل انقضاءها ، فإنّه لا يعتبر الإقرار بالانقضاء إن أقرت في شهر واحد من حين الطلاق مثلاً.
قوله : لا يثبت النسب ؛ وذلك لما تقرّر أنّ أكثر مدة الحمل سنتان، فإذا كان بين الطلاق والولادة أكثر منهما تحقق أنَّ العلوق كان بعد الطلاق، فإنّه إن جعل قبله لزم بقاء الولد في بطنها أكثر من سنتين،
And the lineage of a child of a woman in a revocable divorce is established, even if she gives birth after more than two years, as long as she does not admit that the waiting period has ended; due to the possibility of conception during the waiting period, and the possibility that the woman has an extended period of purity. But if she admits that the waiting period has ended, then gives birth, and between the divorce and the birth there is more than two years, the lineage is not established. He said: "On that... etc." – in addition to what was mentioned, its summary is supporting the establishment of lineage because if the husband knows there was no conception after the valid marital bed, such as if he did not have intercourse with her on that specific night, or he had intercourse and knew that conception preceded the marriage, he would be required to perform li'an with her and deny the child from himself. Since he remained silent, and the possibility of conception during the marital bed exists in one of the mentioned scenarios, we are obliged to exercise precaution in establishing it. He said: "for more" – meaning she gave birth after the divorce for more than two years, even twenty years. He said: "due to the possibility... etc." – its summary: it is possible that intercourse occurred during the waiting period, because the revocable waiting period does not prohibit intercourse, and the woman may have an extended period of purity, meaning the interval between her menses is long; for there is no maximum limit for the longest purity, so the waiting period may not have ended in two years, but in even more, due to the absence of three menses because of extended purity. He said: "with the ending of the waiting period" – and the period may possibly have ended, for her admission of the ending is not considered if she admits it in one month from the time of divorce, for example. He said: "lineage is not established" – because it is established that the maximum period of pregnancy is two years, so if between the divorce and the birth is more than that, it is certain that conception occurred after the divorce, for if it were placed before, it would require the child to remain in her womb for more than two years.
Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage expands on a ruling from the matn concerning the child of a woman in a revocable divorce (raj‘i). The ruling states that the child's lineage is attributed to the husband even if the child is born more than two years after the divorce, as long as the woman does not admit that her iddah (waiting period) has ended. The reason is that intercourse during the iddah is permissible in a revocable divorce, and it is possible that the woman has an unusually long period of purity (tuhr), meaning her menses are far apart, so three menses may not have occurred even after many years. Thus, the iddah may still be ongoing, and any child born during this time is attributed to the husband. However, if the woman admits that her iddah has ended, then the iddah is considered concluded, and if she gives birth after more than two years, the lineage is not established because the maximum pregnancy duration is two years; a child born later cannot be from the husband. The commentator also notes that if the husband suspects the child is not his and he knows he did not have intercourse during the iddah, he should perform li'an (the mutual imprecation) to deny paternity; but if he remains silent, the child's lineage is established due to the possibility of legitimate conception.

Key Terms
عدة الرجعي (ʿiddat al-rajʿī): the waiting period after a revocable divorce, during which the husband may take back his wife without a new marriage contract
ممتدة الطهر (mumtaddat al-ṭuhr): a woman who has an extended period of purity between menses, so her iddah by three menses may take longer than the usual time

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman is divorced revocably. She gives birth four years after the divorce without admitting that her iddah ended. According to the Hanafi school, is the child's lineage established to the husband?
A) Yes, because she never admitted the iddah ended, so it may have continued due to extended purity.
B) No, because four years exceeds the maximum pregnancy of two years.
C) Yes, only if the husband had intercourse during the first two years.
D) No, because the iddah of a revocable divorce only lasts three months.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes lineage for a child born after a revocable divorce even beyond two years, as long as the woman does not admit her iddah ended, due to the possibility of extended purity and permissible intercourse during the iddah.

Establishment of Lineage for Child of Woman in Revocable 'Iddah
Ruling on lineage when birth occurs after two years without admission of iddah end

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lineage of a child born to a woman in revocable iddah beyond two years and explain the reasoning based on ihtiyat and the possibility of extended purity.

Core Idea
Lineage is established even after two years unless the woman admits her iddah ended — caution overrides time.

This lesson examines a key Hanafi ruling on family law: the establishment of lineage (nasab) for a child born to a woman in revocable iddah. Even if the birth occurs more than two years after divorce, the child is attributed to the husband unless the woman herself declares her iddah has ended. The ruling is built on the principles of ihtiyat (caution) in matters of lineage and the recognition that a woman's purity period may be extended, delaying the iddah's completion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State the ruling: lineage is established even if birth occurs after two years, provided the woman does not admit the iddah ended.
2
Understand the reasoning
The reasoning is based on two possibilities: conception during the revocable iddah (which does not prohibit intercourse) and the possibility that the woman has an extended period of purity (mumtaddat al-tuhr), which can prolong the iddah beyond two years.
3
Consider the husband's role
The husband can deny paternity through li'an if he knows with certainty that conception did not occur during the iddah. His silence or failure to perform li'an strengthens the establishment of lineage.
4
Identify the exception
If the woman admits her iddah has ended, and then gives birth after more than two years, lineage is not established because the maximum pregnancy duration (two years) would be exceeded.
5
Evaluate the legal effect
The child's lineage is attributed to the husband, and the mahr (dower) is due to the wife.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is not known whether the marriage is prior to the conception or later, so it must be attributed to coexistence. Since he did not deny the child by li'an, we are not to deny it from the bed with the verification of possibility, so his lineage is established from him, and the mahr is due. Source pages p. 492

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the establishment of lineage (nasab) for a child born to a woman who is in a revocable iddah (iddah al-raj'i). The text begins by stating the ruling: the lineage of such a child is established even if the child is born more than two years after the divorce, provided that the woman does not admit that her iddah has ended. The reasoning is based on the possibility that the conception occurred during the iddah, since revocable iddah does not prohibit intercourse, and also on the possibility that the woman has an extended period of purity between menses, which could delay the completion of the iddah beyond two years. The commentary elaborates by noting that the husband has the option of li'an (mutual imprecation) to deny paternity if he knows with certainty that conception occurred after the divorce. His silence indicates acceptance. However, if the woman admits that the iddah has ended and then gives birth after more than two years, lineage is not established, because the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years, so the conception must have occurred after the iddah. The commentary also clarifies that the admission of iddah completion is itself subject to scrutiny; if she admits it immediately after divorce, it may not be credited because the iddah could not have ended that soon. This ruling demonstrates the Hanafi principle of ihtiyat (caution) in matters of lineage, favoring establishment whenever possible.

Key Terms
معتدة الرجعي (mu'taddah al-raj'i): A woman who is in the waiting period (iddah) after a revocable divorce (talaq raj'i), during which the husband may take her back without a new marriage contract.
علوق ('uluq): Conception; the moment when pregnancy begins.
ممتدة الطهر (mumtaddat al-tuhr): A woman whose period of purity (tuhr) between menses is unusually long, even lasting years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman in revocable iddah gives birth 3 years after the divorce, is the child's lineage established?
A) No, because the maximum pregnancy is 2 years.
B) Yes, unless she has admitted that her iddah ended.
C) Yes, always.
D) No, because the husband may have divorced her.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the lineage of a child born to a woman in revocable iddah is established regardless of the time since divorce, unless the woman admits her iddah has ended.

Effect of Birth Timing on 'Iddah and Reconciliation
Ruling on iddah completion and reconciliation based on birth timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of a woman in revocable iddah who gives birth within or after two years, and explain the rationale based on istihsan.

Core Idea
Birth within two years: ba'in, no raj'a; birth after two years: raj'a established.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya clarifies a crucial distinction in Hanafi family law: the timing of childbirth relative to divorce determines both the completion of 'iddah and the possibility of reconciliation (raj'a). The ruling is based on the maximum pregnancy period of two years and the principle of preferring the more likely scenario while protecting the honor of Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage distinguishes between 'lesser' (al-aqall) and 'greater' (al-akthar). The lesser is birth within two years of divorce; the greater is birth after two years.
The two-year threshold is the Hanafi maximum pregnancy period.
2
Understand the consequence for the woman
In both scenarios, the woman's iddah ends with childbirth. But her status differs: within two years she becomes ba'in (irrevocably divorced); after two years, the husband is deemed to have reconciled.
Iddah of a pregnant woman ends with delivery (Quran 65:4).
3
Analyze the reasoning for the lesser
If birth is within two years, conception could have occurred during marriage or during iddah. Since both are possible, the law chooses the more likely (conception in marriage) to avoid uncertainty, so reconciliation is not established.
Reconciliation requires certainty of intercourse during iddah.
4
Analyze the reasoning for the greater
If birth is after two years, conception during marriage is impossible (would exceed maximum pregnancy). The law rejects the possibility of adultery to protect reputations, so reconciliation is established.
This is an application of istihsan and satt al-'ayb (covering faults).
5
Consider the two periods and false admission
The text also explains that if a woman admits her iddah has passed but then gives birth within six months, her admission is clearly false because she must have been pregnant at the time.
The two periods (al-maddatan) refer to time from divorce to birth and from admission to birth.

Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the legal consequences of childbirth for a woman in revocable iddah. The ruling is summarized in the phrase 'She becomes ba'in in the lesser, and he reconciles in the greater.' The 'lesser' refers to a birth occurring less than two years after the divorce, and the 'greater' refers to a birth occurring more than two years after. If the birth is within two years, the woman becomes ba'in (irrevocably divorced) because her iddah is completed by giving birth. The child's lineage is still established, but the husband is not considered to have reconciled with her (raj'a) because it is possible that the conception occurred during the marriage rather than during the iddah. Reconciliation requires certainty that intercourse took place during the iddah, which is lacking here. If the birth is after two years, the opposite is concluded: the husband is considered to have reconciled her because if the conception had been during the marriage, the pregnancy would have exceeded the maximum duration of two years. The law does not consider the possibility of adultery, as it prefers to protect the reputation of the individuals. The commentary also clarifies that if the woman admits her iddah has passed but then gives birth within six months, her admission is false because she must have been pregnant at the time of admission. This ruling demonstrates the Hanafi reliance on outward signs and probabilities in matters of lineage and marriage.

Key Terms
بائنة (ba'inah): A woman who is irrevocably divorced, meaning the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage contract.
رجعة (raj'a): The husband's act of taking back his wife during the iddah of a revocable divorce, reestablishing the marriage without a new contract.
مدتان (al-maddatan): The two periods: the time from divorce to birth, and the time from admission of iddah completion to birth.

B) She becomes ba'in, but the husband is not considered to have reconciled.
C) She is still in iddah and the husband can take her back.
D) The marriage automatically resumes.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses the two-year maximum pregnancy period to determine whether childbirth completes iddah and establishes reconciliation, balancing probability and the protection of reputation.

Revocably Divorced Woman: Birth Within Two Years Makes Her Ba'in
Ruling when revocably divorced woman gives birth less than two years after talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a revocably divorced woman gives birth less than two years after talaq, and explain why the husband does not have the right of raj'ah.

Core Idea
Birth ends 'iddah and establishes lineage, but raj'ah requires certainty of post-divorce intercourse.

When a revocably divorced woman gives birth, the 'iddah ends, making her ba'in. However, does the husband automatically regain the right to take her back? This lesson examines the Hanafi position that lineage and raj'ah are separate: lineage is presumed from the marriage contract, but raj'ah requires proof that intercourse occurred during the 'iddah. The commentary from al-Hidayah clarifies this subtle but crucial distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The passage considers a revocably divorced woman who gives birth less than two years after the talaq. The ruling is that she becomes ba'in (irrevocably separated).
2
Understand the basis for ending 'iddah
The 'iddah ends with delivery because the Quran (65:4) states that the 'iddah of a pregnant woman ends with birth. The child's lineage is established because conception could have occurred during the marriage.
3
Analyze why raj'ah is not established
Raj'ah would require certainty that intercourse occurred after the divorce. However, the pregnancy could have started before the talaq. Certainty is not established by doubt, so the husband cannot reclaim her without a new marriage.
The principle is 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' (certainty is not removed by doubt).
4
Note potential opposing views
Some may argue that since the child's lineage is established, the marriage must have been ongoing, so raj'ah should be allowed. The Hanafi response distinguishes between lineage (based on possibility) and raj'ah (based on certainty).
5
Apply the principle to modern scenarios
This ruling applies today when a divorcing couple disputes paternity or reunification. The key is to assess timing and the level of certainty regarding intercourse during 'iddah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

يمكن انقضاء العدّة ؛ لأنَّ الحامل لا تحيض، وهذا بخلاف الصورة السابقة، فإنّه لما لم تقر بانقضاء العدة احتمل بقاؤها ، وكونها ممتدة الطهر، ووقوع الوطء حال بالعدة.

That is: if between divorce and birth there is less than two years, she becomes ba'in because it is more likely that the intercourse that caused the pregnancy occurred during the marriage rather than during the 'iddah. The 'iddah can be completed because a pregnant woman does not menstruate, and this differs from the previous scenario where since she did not acknowledge the completion of 'iddah, it is possible that it remains and that she has an extended period of purity and that intercourse occurred during the 'iddah. Commentary
This passage is a commentary expanding on the matn statement: 'She becomes ba'in in the less, and he reconciles in the more.' The author explains that when a revocably divorced woman gives birth less than two years after the divorce, she becomes ba'in (irrevocably separated) because the 'iddah ends with delivery. The lineage of the child is established from the husband, as the child could have been conceived during the marriage or during the 'iddah. However, the husband does not gain the right of raj'ah (return) because that would require certainty that intercourse occurred during the 'iddah, and here there is doubt: the pregnancy could have started before the divorce. The principle is that certainty (here, the marriage bond) is not removed by doubt, and a new right (raj'ah) is not established by doubt. The commentary also clarifies that if the woman had previously acknowledged completion of 'iddah (e.g., by claiming months passed), but then gives birth within six months of that acknowledgement, her statement is shown false and disregarded.

Key Terms
بانت (bānat): She becomes irrevocably divorced (ba'in), meaning the husband cannot take her back without a new marriage.
رجعي (rajʿī): Revocable divorce; the husband can take her back during the 'iddah without a new contract.
علوق (ʿulūq): Conception; the initial attachment of the embryo.

Key Takeaway
Birth within two years of revocable divorce ends 'iddah and establishes paternity, but the husband cannot reclaim his wife without a new marriage due to lack of certainty about post-divorce intercourse.

Revocably Divorced Woman: Birth After Two Years Establishes Raj'ah
Ruling and rational proof for raj'ah by birth after two years

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raj'ah when a revocably divorced woman gives birth more than two years after talaq, explain the rational proof using the maximum pregnancy duration, and apply the principle of satr to avoid accusations of adultery.

Core Idea
A birth two or more years after revocable talaq proves raj'ah, because pregnancy cannot exceed two years.

This passage examines a specific scenario in revocable divorce (talaq raj'i). When a woman in her 'iddah gives birth significantly after the divorce, questions arise about paternity and whether the husband has taken her back. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on the maximum possible duration of pregnancy—two years—and the legal principle of presuming good faith (satr). You will see how rational deduction (dalil aqli) and legal policy combine to establish both the continuation of the marriage and the legitimacy of the child.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the central question
A revocably divorced woman gives birth more than two years after the talaq. The question: Is the husband considered to have taken her back (raj'ah)?
2
Understand the legal impossibility
Conception cannot have occurred during the marriage, because that would imply a pregnancy over two years, which is impossible. So conception must have occurred after divorce, during the 'iddah.
The maximum pregnancy duration in Hanafi law is two years, based on established reports and consensus.
3
Consider and dismiss the alternative
The alternative is that she committed adultery. But legally, this possibility is not acted upon due to the principle of satr (concealment/protection of honor).
Satr presumes good faith and avoids attributing sin without clear evidence.
4
Derive the ruling
Therefore, the husband is deemed to have performed raj'ah, and the child is legitimate.
The same ruling applies if she gives birth exactly two years from the time of divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : وراجع؛ يعني إن ولدت معتدّة الرجعي لأكثر من سنتين من وقتِ الطلاق يحكم بأنّ الزوج راجعها؛ لأنه لا يحتمل هاهنا أن يكون العلوق في النكاح وإلا لزم كون مدة الحمل أكثر من سنتين. واحتمال أن تكون زنت بغير الزوج وحبلت به احتمال لا يحكم به شرعاً ستراً على المسلم والمسلمة، فيحكم بأن زوجها راجعها وحصل العلوق في العدة، وكذا الحكم إذا ولدت لتمام سنتين من وقت الطلاق.
His statement: 'and he reconciles' means: if a woman in revocable 'iddah gives birth more than two years from the time of divorce, it is ruled that the husband has taken her back, because here it is not possible that the conception occurred during the marriage, otherwise the duration of pregnancy would be more than two years. And the possibility that she committed adultery with someone other than her husband and became pregnant is a possibility that is not ruled upon legally, out of protection for the Muslim man and woman. So it is ruled that her husband has taken her back and that conception occurred during the 'iddah. The same ruling applies if she gives birth exactly two years from the time of divorce.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage explains the second part of the matn: 'he reconciles in the more'. When a revocably divorced woman gives birth two years or more after the divorce, the husband is deemed to have taken her back (raj'ah) during the 'iddah. The reasoning is that conception cannot have occurred during the marriage, because that would imply a pregnancy lasting more than two years, which is impossible by consensus (maximum pregnancy duration is two years). The only other possibility is that the husband had intercourse with her during the 'iddah, which constitutes a valid raj'ah. The possibility of adultery is ignored because Islamic law presumes good faith and protects the honor of Muslims; it does not assume zinā without clear evidence. Therefore, the husband's right to take her back is established, and the child's lineage is also from him.

Key Terms
رجعة (rajʿah): The act of taking back a revocably divorced wife during her 'iddah, restoring the marriage without a new contract.
ستر (satr): Concealment; the legal principle of protecting a Muslim's honor by not assuming sinful actions without proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
When a revocably divorced woman gives birth two or more years after talaq, Hanafi law conclusively presumes raj'ah and legitimate paternity, based on the impossibility of longer pregnancy and the principle of satr.

Lineage of Child from Irrevocably Divorced Woman Within Two Years
Ruling on lineage from irrevocably divorced woman within two years

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the lineage of a child born to an irrevocably divorced woman within two years and explain the precautionary reasoning based on possibility of conception during marriage.

Core Idea
For an irrevocably divorced woman, a birth within two years is linked to the husband as a precaution, preserving lineage.

When a woman is irrevocably divorced (ba'in or three divorces), the marriage ends immediately. However, the possibility of pregnancy at the time of divorce remains. The Hanafi school, out of caution (ihtiyat) in matters of lineage, establishes the child's lineage to the ex-husband if the birth occurs within two years of the divorce, provided she has not acknowledged the completion of her 'iddah. This lesson unpacks the timeframe, the reasoning, and the exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Person and the Ruling
Recognize that the passage deals with an irrevocably divorced woman (mut't) and the establishment of her child's lineage from the ex-husband.
The ruling applies only to irrevocable divorce, not revocable.
2
Understand the Timeframe
Note that lineage is established if the birth occurs less than two years from the divorce. If exactly two years or more, it is not established.
The two-year period is the maximum pregnancy duration in the Hanafi school.
3
Apply the Precautionary Principle (Ihtiyat)
Recognize that between six months and two years, conception could have occurred during marriage, so lineage is established as a precaution. Below six months, it is certain.
Ihtiyat is used to protect lineage when there is doubt.
4
Consider the Exception: Acknowledgment of 'Iddah
If the woman has acknowledged the completion of her 'iddah before giving birth, her statement is considered and may affect lineage.
This exception is inherited from earlier rulings in the chapter.
5
Recognize the Consequence for Birth After Two Years
Lineage is not established if birth occurs at or after two years, as it exceeds the maximum possible pregnancy duration.
This is deduced by analogy from the ruling at exactly two years.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(وإن ولدت لتمامهما.

His statement: 'And for an irrevocably divorced woman who gives birth within less than two years [from divorce]' – 'mut't' is in the genitive case, coordinated with 'revocably divorced woman' – meaning: the lineage of the child of a woman divorced with an irrevocable divorce is established if the birth occurs less than two years from the time of irrevocability to the time of birth, because conception during the marriage is possible. (And if she gives birth exactly at the completion of two years...) His statement: 'i.e., it is established...' The gist: an irrevocably divorced woman who gives birth less than two years from the time of divorce, whether less than six months or more, her child's lineage is established from the divorcer. If the interval is less than six months, it is obvious due to certainty of conception during the marriage. If it is more than six months and less than two years, then because the possibility of conception during the marriage exists, it is taken into account as a precaution in matters of lineage. This applies if she has not acknowledged the completion of 'iddah; if she did acknowledge, the ruling is as previously mentioned. This is from al-Fath. His statement: 'at the completion of two years' – he did not mention the ruling if she gives birth after more than two years, because it is known from the ruling of exactly two years: if lineage is not established for birth at exactly two years, it is not established for birth thereafter.
Source pages p. 493

Commentary
This passage addresses an irrevocably divorced woman (mut't) – one who has received a ba'in or threefold divorce. If she gives birth within two years of the divorce, the child's lineage is established from the husband. The reasoning is that conception could have occurred during the marriage. If the birth occurs less than six months after divorce, lineage is certain because conception must have happened during marriage (since minimum pregnancy is six months). If between six months and two years, lineage is still established as a precaution (ihtiyat) in matters of lineage, because it is possible that conception occurred during marriage. However, if she had previously acknowledged the completion of her 'iddah (e.g., by claiming she menstruated), then that statement is considered; if she then gives birth within six months of that acknowledgement, her acknowledgement is shown false. For birth at exactly two years, lineage is not established because it is on the boundary. For birth after two years, it is not established either, as it would exceed the maximum pregnancy duration.

Key Terms
مبتوتة (mut't): A woman divorced with an irrevocable divorce (either ba'in or three divorces).
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precaution; a legal methodology where, in cases of doubt, the ruling that preserves lineage or avoids harm is preferred.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
An irrevocably divorced woman gives birth 18 months after the divorce. She had not previously acknowledged the end of her 'iddah. What is the ruling on the child's lineage?
A) The child's lineage is not established because she is irrevocably divorced.
B) The child's lineage is established from the husband because conception could have occurred during marriage.
C) The child's lineage is established only if the birth was within 6 months.
D) The child's lineage is suspended until a DNA test is done.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes lineage for a child born within two years of an irrevocable divorce as a precautionary measure to protect the child's parentage.

Talaq — Divorce

Lineage of Bain Divorcee's Child: Time Since Divorce
Explaining lineage establishment for a bain divorcee's child based on time since divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lineage establishment for a bain divorcee's child based on time since divorce, and apply the mufta bihi position in the case of birth exactly at two years.

Core Idea
Lineage established if born within two years; at exactly two years, the mufta bihi establishes it — possibility suffices for nasab.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya explains the ruling on establishing lineage for a child born after an irrevocable (bain) divorce. The decisive factor is the maximum gestation period of two years, a foundational Hanafi principle. We will see how the school applies this rule and resolves an internal dispute about the exact two-year mark.

Guided Path
1
Identify the time period relative to divorce
Determine whether the birth occurred less than two years, exactly two years, or more than two years after the final divorce. This categorisation triggers different rulings.
Time is measured from the moment of divorce to the moment of birth.
2
Apply the maximum gestation principle
Recall the Hanafi rule that the maximum pregnancy duration is two years. If a birth occurs less than two years after divorce, conception could have occurred during the marriage — lineage is established.
For intervals less than six months, conception is certain; for intervals between six months and two years, possibility suffices.
3
Recognise the dispute at exactly two years
Note that older texts (Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Hidayah) rule lineage is not established at exactly two years, but later authorities (al-Jawharah) consider this a mistake and rule it established because conception could be simultaneous with divorce.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The later view is the mufta bihi.
4
Understand the reasoning for more than two years
If birth occurs after two years, lineage cannot be established because it would require conception before divorce, making the pregnancy exceed two years — an impossibility.
This is unanimous in the school.
5
Distinguish from revocable divorce
For a revocable (raj'i) divorce, the husband can have intercourse during iddah, so a birth after even two years or more can still be attributed to the marriage if it occurred from that permissible intercourse.
This contrast illustrates how the permissibility of intercourse changes the ruling.

And a woman finally divorced gives birth to less than two [years], and if she gives birth to the completion of both [years], upon the basis that the return [revocability] is a new matter so it is not established by doubt. But if between the divorce and the birth is more than two years, then it must be assumed that the intercourse was during the waiting period, so the return is established. And 'woman finally divorced' gives birth to less than both: 'woman finally divorced' in genitive as a conjunction to 'woman revocably divorced': meaning the lineage of the child of a woman divorced by a final divorce is established if less than two years from the time of finality to the time of birth, due to the possibility of conception during the marriage. And the second: that the return is a new matter which exists after it was not, and the like is not established by doubt, just as something pre-existing does not disappear by doubt. This is the meaning of their statement: certainty is not removed by doubt, and their statement: nothing is established by doubt. This is different from the previous scenario, when she gives birth within two years from the divorce, because there is no repugnance in assuming conception before the divorce, as the period allows it. And different from when a revocably divorced woman gives birth at more than two years or at the end of two years from the divorce, where lineage is established, as has passed, because intercourse during the revocable waiting period is permissible. [1] His statement: 'no' meaning lineage is not established. This is what is mentioned in 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and 'al-Hidayah' and other reliable texts. And it is said: lineage is not established if she gives birth at more than two years for what has passed. But if she gives birth at exactly two years from the divorce, lineage is established, because conception can be imagined at the time of divorce, meaning that the divorce and conception occur at the same moment, neither before nor after, so there is no implication of intercourse after the removal of the marital bed that is established after the divorce, nor the child remaining in the womb for more than two years. (2) And it is mentioned in 'al-Jawharah' and others that this is correct, and that the statement of al-Quduri in this scenario that it is not established is a mistake. And it is said in 'al-Nahr': the truth is to attribute it to a difference in transmissions, due to the concurrence of the texts on its non-establishment.
Source pages p. 494

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on establishing the lineage (nasab) of a child born to a woman who has been divorced by an irrevocable divorce (bain). The key factor is the time elapsed between the divorce and the birth. The commentary opens by stating the rule: if she gives birth less than two years after the divorce, the lineage is established. This is because conception could have occurred during the marriage (if less than six months) or there is a possibility that it did (if between six months and two years), and in matters of lineage, we take precaution by accepting possibilities. If she gives birth at exactly two years or more, the general ruling is that lineage is not established. The reasoning is based on the well-established principle in the Hanafi school that the maximum duration of pregnancy is two years. If the child is born at or after two years, we would have to conclude that conception occurred before the divorce, which would mean the child was in the womb for more than two years, which is impossible. However, there is a significant difference of opinion regarding the case of exactly two years. Al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar and the author of al-Hidayah rule that lineage is not established even at exactly two years, arguing that the moment of divorce cannot be pinpointed for conception. But later scholars like the author of al-Jawharah hold that lineage is established at exactly two years because one can conceive of the conception occurring at the exact same moment as the divorce, thus avoiding the problem of exceeding two years. Al-Jawharah even considers al-Quduri's view a mistake. The commentary also notes that the ruling for a revocably divorced woman is different: her waiting period intercourse is permissible, so if she gives birth after two years, lineage is still established. This passage illustrates how the Hanafi school balances legal principles (certainty, precaution in lineage) and accommodates differences of opinion, ultimately preferring the view that establishes lineage at exactly two years as the mufta bihi (relied-upon position).

Key Terms
مبتوتة (mubattatah): A woman divorced by a final/irrevocable divorce (bain), such as one or two divorces that are not revocable, or three divorces, or khul'.
العلوق (al-ʿulūq): Conception, the moment when pregnancy begins.
أكثر مدة الحمل (akthar muddat al-ḥaml): The maximum duration of pregnancy, established in the Hanafi school as two years.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman receives a final (bain) divorce on January 1, 2020. She gives birth on January 1, 2022. According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, is the child's lineage established to the divorcer?
A) Yes, because the birth occurs exactly at two years, and conception could be at the moment of divorce.
B) No, because the maximum pregnancy is two years, so the child must have been conceived after the divorce.
C) Yes, because a bain divorcee can still have intercourse during iddah.
D) No, because lineage after a final divorce is never established.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a child born to a bain divorcee within two years of divorce has established lineage; at exactly two years, the later preferred view also establishes it, prioritizing possibility over certainty.

Talaq — Divorce

Lineage from Irrevocable Divorce After Two Years: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Establishes the ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on child's lineage from irrevocably divorced woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority Hanafi ruling on lineage for a child born to an irrevocably divorced woman after two years, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding birth exactly at the two-year mark.

Core Idea
Child born two years after irrevocable divorce: lineage not established, but some say exactly at two years it may be.

This lesson examines a nuanced ruling within Hanafi fiqh: the lineage (nasab) of a child born to a woman who has been irrevocably divorced (bāʾin). The core issue is whether the passage of two full years from the divorce severs any possibility of attributing the child to the former husband. While the majority of authoritative texts hold that lineage is not established, a minority of later scholars argue for an exception if the birth occurs precisely at the completion of two years. Understanding this dispute requires careful consideration of the maximum pregnancy period and the moment of conception relative to the divorce.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling from Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Hidayah: if an irrevocably divorced woman gives birth at the end of two years or more, lineage is not established.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Identify the dissenting view
Note that some Hanafi scholars (e.g., Qadi Khan, al-Jawharah) hold that if the birth occurs exactly at the completion of two years, lineage is established.
This dispute is within the Hanafi school, not with another madhhab.
3
Analyze the dissenting proof
The dissent argues that conception could occur at the exact moment of divorce, before the marital bond (firash) is fully removed. Thus intercourse at that moment would be lawful and pregnancy could last exactly two years.
They rely on the possibility of simultaneous conception and divorce.
4
Examine the majority response
The majority counters that the divorce immediately removes the firash, making intercourse unlawful. Attributing the child would necessitate conception after divorce, implying a pregnancy beyond two years, which contradicts the established maximum.
The majority view is considered stronger in the primary texts.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The practical difference: under the majority, a child born exactly two years after irrevocable divorce is not attributed to the ex-husband; under the minority, the child is attributed. This affects inheritance, custody, and other rights.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the majority position of non-establishment.

Source Text

Chapter of Divorce, Section on Establishing Lineage and Custody. (1) For more than that by the primary method. Al-Fasih al-Harawi interpreted the author's words to include both situations, such that his saying 'its completion by the passage of two years' is general, whether it is at the end of two years or more. The conclusion is that if an irrevocably divorced woman gives birth to a child at the end of two years from the time of divorce or more, his lineage is not established from the divorcer; because if it were established, it would necessitate that conception occurred before the divorce, since intercourse is not permissible after it if it is irrevocable. And it is said: lineage is not established if she gives birth after more than two years for what has passed. As for if she gives birth at the completion of two years from the time of divorce, then lineage is established because conception at the time of divorce is conceivable, such that his divorce and conception occur at the same moment, neither before nor after. Hence there is no necessity for intercourse after the removal of the bed that is established after divorce, nor for the child remaining in the womb for more than two years. And it is said in al-Nahr: the truth is to interpret it as a difference in narrations, because the texts concur on its non-establishment. Source pages p. 495

Commentary
This passage from the sharh (commentary) on the matn discusses the ruling on the lineage (nasab) of a child born to a woman who has been irrevocably divorced (mubattatah). The author first presents the established ruling from Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Hidayah: if the woman gives birth at the end of two years from the time of divorce or more, the child's lineage is not attributed to the ex-husband. The reasoning is that to attribute the child to him would require conception after the divorce, but intercourse after an irrevocable divorce is unlawful (haram). Moreover, the maximum period of pregnancy in Hanafi fiqh is two years, so any longer would contradict that principle. The passage then distinguishes this from two other cases: (1) if she gives birth in less than two years, lineage is established because it is possible that conception occurred before divorce; (2) if the divorce was revocable (raj‘i), lineage is established even after two years because intercourse is lawful during the revocable 'iddah. The commentary then notes an intra-Hanafi dispute: some scholars (including al-Jawharah and Qadi Khan) hold that if the woman gives birth exactly at the completion of two years from the divorce, lineage is established. Their argument is that conception could have occurred at the very moment of divorce, before the marital bed (firash) was removed. The text from al-Nahr suggests this divergence may reflect different narrations within the school. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to the matn is that lineage is not established, but the issue is not without scholarly debate.

Key Terms
مبتوتة (mubattatah): A woman who has been irrevocably divorced (with a bain divorce), where the husband cannot return to her without a new marriage contract.
علوق ('uluq): Conception (the moment of fertilization). In this context, it refers to the time the child is conceived relative to the divorce.
فراش (firash): The marital bed; metaphorically, the marriage bond. 'Zawal al-firash' means the removal of the marital bond due to divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi position (as per al-Quduri and al-Hidayah), what is the ruling on lineage if an irrevocably divorced woman gives birth exactly two years after the divorce?
A) Lineage is established because conception could have occurred at the moment of divorce.
B) Lineage is not established because it would require conception after divorce and a pregnancy exceeding two years.
C) Lineage is established only if the ex-husband claims the child.
D) Lineage is not established because the 'iddah has ended.

Key Takeaway
The majority Hanafi ruling is that a child born two years or more after an irrevocable divorce is not attributed to the ex-husband, though a minority grants an exception at the exact two-year mark.

Exception: Lineage Established by Claim and Conditions of Shubha
Defines the exception where child's lineage is established if husband claims, with conditions of shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of shubha that allow lineage to be established by the ex-husband's claim and explain why shubha fi al-fi‘l is insufficient.

Core Idea
Lineage is established by the ex-husband's claim only if there was a chance of intercourse under shubha in the subject or contract—not just shubha in the act.

In the previous lesson, we learned the general rule: a child born to an irrevocably divorced woman after two full years of iddah is not linked to the ex-husband. However, the Hanafi school recognizes an exception: if the ex-husband voluntarily claims the child, the lineage is established. But this exception is not unconditional; it requires that there be a possibility that intercourse occurred under a legal ambiguity (shubha). This passage unpacks the types of shubha that satisfy this condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling and the exception
Begin by noting the default: lineage is not established for a child born to a mubattatah after two years. Then locate the exception: 'illa bi da‘wah' (except by claim). Understand that this exception allows lineage if the ex-husband claims the child.
The exception is affirmative; it overrides the default negation.
2
Recognize the problem and the solution via shubha
The apparent contradiction: how can lineage be established when intercourse is impossible (before marriage or after divorce)? The text explains that intercourse could have occurred during iddah under a shubha (legal ambiguity). This resolves the impossibility.
Shubha creates a legal possibility that saves the connection.
3
Classify the three types of shubha
The passage divides shubha into: shubha fi al-mahal (in the subject), shubha fi al-fi‘l (in the act), and shubha fi al-‘aqd (in the contract). Identify each type from the examples given (e.g., intercourse with son's slave girl is shubha fi al-mahal; kinayah divorce is shubha fi al-‘aqd).
Shubha fi al-mahal concerns doubt about the permissibility of the woman herself; shubha fi al-‘aqd concerns doubt about the validity of a contract.
4
Determine which types are effective for lineage
The text explicitly states that lineage is established only with shubha fi al-mahal or shubha fi al-‘aqd. Shubha fi al-fi‘l does not suffice. Understand the reasoning: shubha in the subject or contract goes to the root of permissibility, making the relationship plausible; shubha in the act is weaker.
This is a key Hanafi distinction that affects many rulings.
5
Apply the condition to a scenario
Given a case where the ex-husband claims a child, analyze whether intercourse during iddah could have occurred under a valid shubha. If the shubha is only in the act (e.g., forgetting the prohibition), his claim does not establish lineage.
The claim alone is not sufficient; the underlying possibility of lawful/shubha intercourse must be of a specific type.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1]قوله : إلا بدعوة ; - هو بكسر الدال المهملة - , يقال : لادّعاءَ النَّسب, يعني : لا يثبتُ النَّسب فيما إذا ولدت المبتوتة لتمام سنتين أو أكثر إذا ادّعاه المطلق ونسبه إلى نفسه, فحينئذ يثبت النسب منه. [2]قوله : ويحمل ... الخ ; دفع لما يقال : كيف يثبتُ النَّسب في هذه الصورة بدعوته مع عدم إمكان العلوق قبل النكاح ولا بعده, أما قبله فللزوم زيادة مدة الحمل على سنتين, وأما بعده فلحرمة الوطء في عدة الطلاق البائن, وحاصل الدفع أنه يمكن وجود الوطء حال العدة بالشبهة. [3] قوله : بشبهة ; اعترض عليه : بأنّ الوطء في العدة بالشبهة إن كان فإنّما يكون بشبهة في الفعل, وبه لا يثبت النَّسب , وإنّما يثبتُ إذا كان الوطء بشبهة في المحل أو بشبهة في العقد. وأجيب عنه : بأن وطءَ المعتدة يمكن بشبهة المحلّ أيضاً, ويمكن وطء المطلقة بالثلاث أو على مال في العدّة بشبهة العقد أيضاً, فيثبتُ النَّسب هناك بدعوته, وإن لم يثبت في صورة الشبهة في الفعل. وتوضيحه : إن الوطء الحرام الذي يكون بشبهة فيسقط به حد الزنا, وإن وجب التعزير في بعض صوره على أقسام ثلاثة بحسب انقسام الشبهات : الأول : أن يكون بشبهة في المحلّ, بأن يقوم هناك دليل ناف للحرمة, وثبت لحل المحل, وإن كان ذلك دليلاً ضعيفاً فيورث ذلك اشتباهاً, فيكون وطؤه مبنياً عليه, وفي مثل هذا الوطء يثبتُ النِّسبُ بدعوته, وذلك كوطء أمة ابنه اغتراراً بحديث : «أنت ومالك لأبيك»(1). ووطء معتدته بالطلاق البائن ما دون الثلاث بألفاظ الكنايات , اغتراراً بما اختاره بعض الصحابة من أنَّ الكنايات رواجع. الثاني: أن يكون بشبهة في الفعل, بأن يقع للمواطئ اشتباه في حرمة نفس ذلك ;
[1] His saying: 'except by claim' – it is with kasra on the dal, meaning: for claiming lineage, i.e., lineage is not established when the mubattatah gives birth at the completion of two years or more, unless the divorcer claims it and attributes it to himself, in which case lineage is established from him. [2] His saying: 'and it is interpreted...' etc. This is a repudiation of what is said: how can lineage be established in this case by his claim when conception is impossible before the marriage or after it? Before it, because it would necessitate increasing the pregnancy period beyond two years; after it, because intercourse is forbidden during the iddah of an irrevocable divorce. The essence of the repudiation is that intercourse during the iddah with shubha can occur. [3] His saying: 'with shubha' – an objection was raised: that intercourse during the iddah with shubha, if it occurs, is only shubha in the act (fi‘l), and with that lineage is not established. Rather, it is established only if the intercourse is with shubha in the subject (mahal) or with shubha in the contract (‘aqd). The answer is: intercourse with a woman in iddah can occur with shubha in the subject as well, and intercourse with a thrice-divorced woman or one divorced for payment during the iddah can also occur with shubha in the contract. Hence lineage is established there by his claim, even if it is not established in the case of shubha in the act. The clarification: Unlawful intercourse that occurs with shubha, which lifts the hadd of zina (even if ta‘zir is obligatory in some cases), is of three types according to the division of shubuhat. First: shubha fi al-mahal – when there is evidence negating the prohibition, establishing the permissibility of the subject, even if the evidence is weak, causing confusion. In such intercourse, lineage is established by his claim, such as intercourse with his son's slave girl, deceived by the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father', and intercourse with his woman in iddah of an irrevocable divorce less than three, using kinayah expressions, deceived by what some Companions chose that kinayah are revocable. Second: shubha fi al-fi‘l – when the person engaging in intercourse has confusion about the prohibition of that act itself.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the exception to the general ruling: 'except by claim' (illa bi da‘wah). The commentator explains that even though the general rule negates lineage for a child born to a mubattatah after two years, if the ex-husband voluntarily claims the child as his own, the lineage is established (ثبت النسب بدعوته). However, this is not unconditional; it requires that there be a possibility of lawful or shubha-based intercourse during the 'iddah. The commentator then addresses an objection: how can lineage be established through a claim when no lawful intercourse could have occurred? The answer is that intercourse may have occurred under a shubha (legal ambiguity). The text then discusses three types of shubha in Hanafi jurisprudence: (1) shubha fi al-mahal – ambiguity concerning the subject (e.g., believing a woman is lawful to have sex with due to a weak but accepted evidence), (2) shubha fi al-fi‘l – ambiguity concerning the act itself (the passage cuts off but this type is mentioned), and (3) shubha fi al-‘aqd – ambiguity in the contract (mentioned in the reply). The key point: only shubha fi al-mahal and shubha fi al-‘aqd establish lineage upon the husband's claim; shubha fi al-fi‘l does not. The commentator illustrates with examples: a man having intercourse with his son's slave girl relying on the hadith 'You and your wealth belong to your father' (a weak but relied-upon statement), and a man using kinayah (ambiguous words) in divorcing his wife, relying on the view of some Companions that such kinayah are revocable (so he thought she was still his wife). These examples involve shubha fi al-mahal.

Key Terms
دعوة (da‘wah): The claim of paternity made by the ex-husband, acknowledging the child as his own.
شبهة (shubha): Legal ambiguity that creates doubt about the prohibition of an act. In this context, it refers to circumstances that make intercourse during the iddah possibly not sinful, enough to attribute the child to the man if he claims it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In what type of shubha does the Hanafi school accept that lineage can be established by the ex-husband's claim?
A) Shubha fi al-fi‘l only
B) Shubha fi al-mahal and shubha fi al-‘aqd
C) Shubha fi al-fi‘l and shubha fi al-mahal
D) All three types of shubha

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recognizes an exception to the general rule of non-lineage: when the ex-husband claims the child, and there is a possibility of intercourse under shubha in the subject or contract, the lineage is established; shubha in the act alone does not suffice.

Lineage Establishment with Shubha in 'Iddah
Explaining when lineage is established for a divorced woman claiming shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of shubha and state which ones establish lineage according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Lineage is established only if shubha is in the object or contract, not merely in the act.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah sharpens the ruling on lineage for a mubattatah. The core issue: a child born up to two years after divorce can be attributed to the ex-husband, but only if he claims paternity and there was intercourse with a legal doubt (shubha). The author, Ibn al-'Ayni, refutes an objection by classifying shubha and showing which kinds validate lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi rule for lineage of a child born to a mubattatah (irrevocably divorced woman) within two years.
The matn says: lineage is not established unless the husband claims it (da'wa).
2
Understand the role of da'wa
Why is the husband's claim necessary? The author explains that the default rule is non-establishment, but the claim can override that if shubha is possible.
Da'wa is the husband's active assertion of paternity.
3
Analyse the objection and answer
How can lineage be established when intercourse before divorce is too early and after is forbidden? The answer: intercourse during 'iddah with shubha is possible.
This sets up the classification of shubha.
4
Classify the three types of shubha
List and define: shubha fi al-mahall (doubt in object), shubha fi al-fi'l (doubt in act), shubha fi al-`aqd (doubt in contract).
Each has a different legal effect on lineage.
5
Apply the classification to lineage
Determine which types establish lineage: only first and third, not second.
Memorize: lineage follows shubha in object or contract, not mere act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلا بدعوة، ويحمل على وطئها بشبهة في العدة. قوله : إلا بدعوة ; - هو بكسر الدال المهملة - ، يقال : لادّعاءَ النَّسب، يعني : لا يثبتُ النَّسب فيما إذا ولدت المبتوتة لتمام سنتين أو أكثر إذا ادّعاه المطلق ونسبه إلى نفسه، فحينئذ يثبت النسب منه. قوله : ويحمل ... الخ ; اعترض عليه : بأنّ الوطء في العدة بالشبهة إن كان فإنّما يكون بشبهة في الفعل، وبه لا يثبت النَّسب ، وإنّما يثبتُ إذا كان الوطء بشبهة في المحل أو بشبهة في العقد. وأجيب عنه : بأن وطءَ المعتدة يمكن بشبهة المحلّ أيضاً، ويمكن وطء المطلقة بالثلاث أو على مال في العدّة بشبهة العقد أيضاً، فيثبتُ النَّسب هناك بدعوته، وإن لم يثبت في صورة الشبهة في الفعل. وتوضيحه : إن الوطء الحرام الذي يكون بشبهة فيسقط به حد الزنا، وإن وجب التعزير في بعض صوره على أقسام ثلاثة بحسب انقسام الشبهات : الأول : أن يكون بشبهة في المحلّ، بأن يقوم هناك دليل ناف للحرمة، وثبت لحل المحل، وإن كان ذلك دليلاً ضعيفاً فيورث ذلك اشتباهاً، فيكون وطؤه مبنياً عليه، وفي مثل هذا الوطء يثبتُ النِّسبُ بدعوته، وذلك كوطء أمة ابنه اغتراراً بحديث : «أنت ومالك لأبيك». ووطء معتدته بالطلاق البائن ما دون الثلاث بألفاظ الكنايات ، اغتراراً بما اختاره بعض الصحابة من أنَّ الكنايات رواجع. الثاني: أن يكون بشبهة في الفعل، بأن يقع للمواطئ اشتباه في حرمة نفس ذلك الفعل أي الوطء، ويظنّه حلالاً لوجه لاح له من دون أن يقوم دليل دال على إباحة محل الوطء ; أي الموطوءة، وذلك كوطء أمة أبويه اغتراراً بالانبساط التام بين الولد والأبوين في الانتفاع بالأملاك، وفي مثله لا يثبت النسب، وإن ادعاه. الثالث : الشبهة بالعقد، فيظن الوطء به حلالاً، وإن كان ذلك العقد لغـواً وفاسداً ; كالوطء بمعتدته بالثلاث أو على مال بعد النكاح بها في العدة، وإن شئت زيادة التفصيل في هذا المبحث الجليل فارجع إلى رسالتي : «القول الجازم في سقوط الحدّ بنكاح المحارم». أي إن جاءت لتمام سنتين من وقتِ الفرقة لم يثبت ; لأنَّ الحمل حادث بعد الطلاق، فلا يكون منه ; لأن وطأها حرام، وقوله : إلا بدعوة ; لأنه التزمه ، وله وجه بأن وطئها بشبهة في العدة
Except with a claim, and it is construed as intercourse with a doubt during the 'iddah. His statement: 'except with a claim' – it is with a kasra on the dal, meaning: claim of lineage, i.e., lineage is not established in the case where a woman divorced irrevocably gives birth at the completion of two years or more if the divorcer claims it and attributes it to himself, then the lineage is established from him. His statement: 'and it is construed...' etc.; a refutation of what is said: how can lineage be established in this situation by his claim when conception before marriage is impossible, nor after it? As for before, because the period of pregnancy would exceed two years; as for after, because of the prohibition of intercourse during the 'iddah of an irrevocable divorce. The gist of the refutation is that intercourse can occur during the 'iddah with doubt. His statement: 'with doubt' – an objection was raised: that intercourse during the 'iddah with doubt is only a doubt in the act, and by it lineage is not established; rather it is established only if the intercourse is with a doubt in the object or a doubt in the contract. The answer is: intercourse with a woman in 'iddah can also be with a doubt in the object, and intercourse with a woman divorced by triple divorce or for compensation during the 'iddah can also be with a doubt in the contract, so lineage is established there by his claim, even if it is not established in the case of doubt in the act. Explanation: unlawful intercourse that occurs with doubt such that the hadd penalty for fornication is dropped, though ta'zir may be required in some forms, is of three types according to the division of doubts: First: that it is with a doubt in the object, such that there exists some evidence negating prohibition, establishing the permissibility of the object, albeit weak, causing confusion, so intercourse is based on it; in such intercourse lineage is established by his claim, such as intercourse with his son's slave woman relying on the hadith: 'You and your property belong to your father', and intercourse with his wife divorced irrevocably by less than triple divorce using allusive words relying on the choice of some Companions that allusive words are revocable. Second: that it is with a doubt in the act, such that the one having intercourse is confused about the prohibition of that very act, i.e., the intercourse, and thinks it is permissible for a reason that occurs to him without any evidence indicating the permissibility of the object of intercourse, i.e., the woman; such as intercourse with the slave woman of his parents relying on the complete familiarity between a child and parents in using properties; in such a case lineage is not established, even if he claims it. Third: doubt in the contract, where he thinks intercourse is permissible through it, even if that contract is void and invalid; such as intercourse with his wife divorced by triple divorce or for compensation after marriage to her in the 'iddah. If you wish further detail on this important topic, refer to my treatise: 'The Decisive Word on the Dropping of the Hadd Penalty for Marriage to Mahram Relatives.' He said: if she came with the child at the completion of two years from the time of separation, it is not established, because the pregnancy occurred after divorce and so is not from him, for his intercourse with her is prohibited. His statement: 'except with a claim' because he has accepted it, and there is a position that his intercourse with her was with doubt during the 'iddah.
Source pages p. 496

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Wiqayah expands on the ruling that a child born to a divorced woman can be attributed to her ex-husband if he claims it, even if the birth occurs up to two years after divorce, provided that there was intercourse with shubha during the 'iddah. The author first explains the matn's phrase 'except with a claim,' meaning the husband must affirmatively claim paternity. Then he addresses an objection: how can the child be from him if intercourse could not have happened before or after? He resolves this by asserting the possibility of intercourse during the 'iddah with a shubha (doubt) that makes the intercourse less than fully forbidden. He then classifies shubha into three types: (1) shubha fi al-mahall (doubt in the object), where the man mistakenly believes the woman is permissible; (2) shubha fi al-fi'l (doubt in the act), where he mistakenly believes the act itself is permissible; (3) shubha fi al-`aqd (doubt in the contract), where he acts under a defective contract. The key ruling: lineage is established only in the first and third types, not in the second. The passage ends by confirming the basic rule: if the child is born two years after separation, lineage is not established unless claimed, and then only if shubha is possible.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): Doubt or uncertainty that affects the legal ruling; here classified into three types: in the object, in the act, and in the contract.
مبتوتة (mubattatah): A woman divorced irrevocably (bain), i.e., with a divorce that does not allow return during 'iddah without a new marriage.
دعوة (da'wa): Claim or assertion of paternity by the ex-husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In which type of shubha is lineage established according to the Hanafi school?
A) Shubha fi al-mahall only
B) Shubha fi al-fi'l only
C) Shubha fi al-mahall and shubha fi al-`aqd
D) All three types

Key Takeaway
For lineage of a child born to an irrevocably divorced woman, the Hanafi school requires the husband's claim and that intercourse during 'iddah occurred with a shubha in the object or contract, not merely a shubha in the act.

Lineage for a Minor Girl's Child After Divorce
Ruling on lineage when a divorced minor girl gives birth less than nine months after divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a murahiqah's child is attributed to the ex-husband and explain the rationale using the 'iddah and minimum pregnancy periods.

Core Idea
A murahiqah's child born within nine months of divorce is attributed to the ex-husband.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hanafi family law: a divorced minor girl (murahiqah) who gives birth. The crucial factor is timing. The Hanafi school derives a clear ruling by combining the murahiqah's three-month 'iddah with the minimum pregnancy period of six months, producing a nine-month window.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and legal context
We have a divorced murahiqah – a girl between nine and fifteen years with no signs of puberty. The divorce can be any type (revocable or irrevocable).
The murahiqah's 'iddah is three months, not three menstrual cycles.
2
Determine the time constraint
The child must be born less than nine months from the time of divorce. Birth at nine months or later does not establish lineage.
The matn explicitly says 'and at nine months (no)'.
3
Understand the rationale
The nine-month limit is the sum of the murahiqah's 'iddah (3 months) and the minimum pregnancy (6 months).
This is a rational deduction (dalil aqli).
4
Conclude the ruling
If birth occurs within that window, the child's lineage is attributed to the husband; otherwise it is not.
The husband's acknowledgment is also considered, but the timing is primary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومراهقة أتت به لأقل من تسعة أشهر ولتسعة (لا): ومراهقة : بالجرّ عطف على مبتوتة : أي يثبت نسب ولد مطلقة مراهقة أتت بولد لأقل من تسعة أشهر من وقت الطلاق. والمراد بالمراهقة : صبية يجامع مثلها وهي في سن يمكن أن تكون بالغة : أي تسع سنين فصاعداً ، ولم يظهر فيها علامات البلوغ ; لأنَّ ثلاثة أشهرٍ . عدتها، وستة أشهر أقل مدة الحمل. [١]قوله : الفرقة ; بالطلاق البائن ثلاثاً كان أو ما دونه أو بالخلع أو بغيرهما. [٢]قوله : لأنّه ; يعني أنّ المطلقَ التزم نسبه بادعائه، والمرء يؤخذ بإقراره. [٣]قوله : بالمراهقة ; - بكسر الهاء - يقال : راهق الغلام فهو مراهق ، وراهقت البنت فهي مراهقة : إذا قاربت البلوغ ، بأن بلغت سن البلوغ، ولم يوجد في البلوغ. [٤]قوله : فصاعداً ; أي أكثر من تسع إلى خمسة عشر، فإنه إذا وصلت إلى خمسة عشر ولم توجد فيه آثار البلوغ فهي بالغة شرعاً، فإنَّ سن البلوغ في حق الرجل والمرأة كليهما هو خمسة عشر على الصحيح. [٥]قوله : أقل مدة الحمل ; قال الشارح الهروي : يثبت نسب مراهقة إذا طلقها زوجها طلاقاً بائناً أو رجعيّا وأتت به لأقل من تسعة أشهر من وقت الطلاق
And a minor girl (murahiqah) who brings a child at less than nine months, and at nine months (no). Murahiqah is in the genitive, conjoined to 'mubattatah': i.e., the lineage of a child of a divorced minor girl is established if she gives birth less than nine months from the time of divorce. What is meant by murahiqah: a girl who is of an age to be penetrated, and she is at an age that could be puberty: i.e., nine years and above, and no signs of puberty have appeared; because her 'iddah is three months, and the minimum period of pregnancy is six months. [1] His statement: 'separation' – by irrevocable divorce, be it triple or less, or by khul' or other. [2] His statement: 'because he' – meaning that the divorcer has accepted the lineage by his claim, and a person is held to his acknowledgment. [3] His statement: 'with murahiqah' – with a kasra on the ha', it is said: the boy became murahiq, so he is murahiq, and the girl became murahiqah, so she is murahiqah: when she approaches puberty, i.e., she has reached the age of puberty but no signs of puberty appear. [4] His statement: 'and above' – i.e., from nine to fifteen, because when she reaches fifteen and no signs of puberty appear, she is legally an adult; indeed the age of puberty for both men and women is fifteen according to the correct view. [5] His statement: 'minimum period of pregnancy' – al-Sharih al-Harawi said: the lineage of a murahiqah is established if her husband divorces her, irrevocably or revocably, and she gives birth less than nine months from the time of divorce.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This section addresses the special case of a murahiqah – a girl approaching puberty, specifically between nine and fifteen years without signs of puberty. If she is divorced and gives birth less than nine months after the divorce, her child's lineage is attributed to the ex-husband. The reasoning is that her 'iddah is three months (since she has not reached full puberty) and the minimum period of pregnancy is six months, totaling nine months. Thus, birth within that period can be attributed to the husband. The notes clarify terms: 'separation' includes all types of divorce; the husband's claim (even if only verbal) is sufficient; the age range of murahiqah; and the confirmation from al-Sharih al-Harawi.

Key Terms
مراهقة (murahiqah): A girl approaching puberty, aged between nine and fifteen without signs of puberty.
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period after divorce; for a murahiqah, it is three months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the nine-month period significant for establishing the lineage of a murahiqah's child?
A) Because it is the maximum 'iddah for a minor.
B) Because it is the sum of her three-month 'iddah and six-month minimum pregnancy.
C) Because it is the average human gestation period.
D) Because it matches the age of the girl.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school attributes the child of a divorced murahiqah to the ex-husband if born within the combined 'iddah and minimum gestation period of nine months.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Establishing Lineage of a Child Born to a Divorced Minor (Murāhiqah)
Ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute on lineage timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the maximum period after divorce for establishing the lineage of a child born to a divorced minor, explain the majority view and Abu Yusuf's dissent, and apply the rule by calculating the 9-month period.

Core Idea
For a divorced minor, the child's lineage to the ex-husband is established only if born within 9 months of divorce—3 months iddah plus 6 months minimum pregnancy.

This passage from the 'Umdat al-Ri'aya commentary on al-Wiqaya addresses a specific but important scenario: a young wife who has not reached puberty (murāhiqah) is divorced, and later gives birth. When can the child be attributed to her former husband? The answer hinges on the interplay between the legislated waiting period ('iddah) of three months for a non-menstruating woman and the minimum duration of pregnancy. The Hanafi school's majority relies on these fixed periods to determine lineage, while Imam Abu Yusuf allows a longer window. Let's examine the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the ruling
Read the matn: 'A minor approaching puberty who gives birth at less than nine months [from divorce], and at nine months, no.' This tells you the basic rule: if birth <9 months, lineage established; if ≥9 months, not established.
The passage also mentions an exception when the husband claims the child (da'wa).
2
Understand the legal basis
The iddah for a minor is 3 months (Quran 65:4). The minimum pregnancy duration is 6 months (by medical and legal inference). Combined, 9 months is the maximum possible window for the child to be conceived from the ex-husband.
This is a dalil aqli - rational deduction based on the revealed text and natural limits.
3
Apply the calculation
If the child is born at 7 months, then 3 months (iddah) + 4 months (pregnancy) = 7 months, within the window. If at 10 months, 3 + 7 = 10, exceeding the limit, so not from the husband.
The passage states that after six months from divorce, the iddah is definitively over, so any pregnancy must be from a subsequent relationship.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf disagrees: he allows lineage up to 2 years (irrevocable divorce) or 27 months (revocable) because he considers the possibility of a longer pregnancy.
The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) relies on the certainty of the fixed periods, while Abu Yusuf allows for exceptional possibilities.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text presents Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's view as the default and quotes Abu Yusuf as an alternative. The relied-upon fatwa position is the majority view.
Always check the tarjih: the stronger view is based on definitive texts and medical reality.

مراهقة أتت به لأقل من تسعة أشهر ولتسعة لا
أي إن جاءت لتمام سنتين من وقتِ الفرقة لم يثبت؛ لأنَّ الحمل حادث بعد الطلاق، فلا يكون منه؛ لأن وطأها حرام، وقوله : إلا بدعوة؛ لأنه التزمه، وله وجه بأن وطئها بشبهة في العدة.
ومراهقة أتت به لأقل من تسعة أشهر ولتسعة (لا): ومراهقة : بالجرّ عطف على مبتوتة : أي يثبت نسب ولد مطلقة مراهقة أتت بولد لأقل من تسعة أشهر من وقتِ الطلاق.
والمراد بالمراهقة" : صبية يجامع مثلها وهي في سن يمكن أن تكون بالغة : أي تسع سنين فصاعداً ، ولم يظهر فيها علامات البلوغ ؛ لأنَّ ثلاثة أشهرٍ . عدتها، وستة أشهر أقل مدة الحمل)
أي الوطء، ويظنّه حلالاً لوجه لاح له من دون أن يقوم دليل دال على إباحة محل الوطء ؛ أي الموطوءة، وذلك كوطء أمة أبويه اغتراراً بالانبساط التام بين الولد والأبوين في الانتفاع بالأملاك، وفي مثله لا يثبت النسب، وإن ادعاه.

[٢] قوله : لأنّه ؛ يعني أنّ المطلقَ التزم نسبه بادعائه، والمرء يؤخذ بإقراره. [٤] قوله : فصاعداً ؛ أي أكثر من تسع إلى خمسة عشر، فإنه إذا وصلت إلى خمسة عشر ولم توجد فيه آثار البلوغ فهي بالغة شرعاً، فإنَّ سن البلوغ في حق الرجل والمرأة كليهما هو خمسة عشر على الصحيح.
