فيحمل
ولو أتت به لتسعة أشهر فصاعداً لا يثبت النسب عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ؛ لأنَّ لانقضاء عدتها جهة معينة، وهو ثلاثة أشهر ، وصفة الصغر باقية باليقين، وهي منافية للحمل لعدم مائها ، فإذا مضت ستة أشهر فقد حكم الشرع بانقضاء العدة، على أمر حادث بعدها. لأنه بقي إما ستة أشهر أو أزيد فيحتمل أن يكون العلوق من غير الزوج، فيقع الشك في نسبه، فلا يثبت عن الزوج ولا ينقطع أيضاً عن أصله ؛ لاحتمال التزوج بالآخر، ثم ولدت منه لأقل زمان الولادة ؛ لاحتمال كون النكاح الآخر والإنزال معاً وإن بقي أكثر من ستة أشهر فظاهر». انتهى.
وفي «تبيين الحقائق شرح كنز الدقائق للزيلعي هذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ، والرجعي والبائن فيه سواء، وقال أبو يوسف الله : يثبت النسب منه إلى سنتين إذا كان بائناً، وإن كان رجعيّاً يثبت منه إلى سبعة وعشرين شهراً ، وبعده لا يثبت، وهذا إذا لم تقر بالحبل ولا بانقضاء العدة.
وأما إذا أقرت بالحبل فهو إقرار منها بالبلوغ، فيقبل قولها، فصارت كالكبيرة في حق ثبوتِ نسبه، وإن أقرّت بانقضاء العدّة بعد ثلاثة أشهر، ثم جاءت بولد لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار، ولأقل من تسعة أشهر من وقت الطلاق، يثبت نسبه لظهور كذبها بيقين». انتهى.
Book of Divorce, Chapter on Establishing Lineage and Custody. A minor girl approaching puberty who gives birth at less than nine months [from divorce], and at nine months, no. That is, if she comes at the completion of two years from the time of separation, it is not established; because the pregnancy occurred after the divorce, so it cannot be from him; because intercourse with her is prohibited. And his statement: 'except by claim' because he acknowledged it, and it has a basis that he had intercourse with her under a semblance of right during the waiting period. And 'a minor approaching puberty who gives birth at less than nine months and at nine months (no)': 'minor' is in the genitive as a conjunction to 'divorced woman': that is, the lineage of the child of a divorced minor approaching puberty who gives birth less than nine months from the time of divorce is established. And what is meant by 'minor approaching puberty': a girl who is capable of intercourse and at an age where she could have reached puberty: i.e., nine years and above, and signs of puberty have not appeared in her; because three months is her waiting period, and six months is the minimum duration of pregnancy. That is, the intercourse, and he thinks it is lawful for a reason that appears to him without clear evidence indicating the permissibility of the place of intercourse, i.e., the woman, such as intercourse with the slave girl of his parents, deceived by the complete familiarity between the child and parents in benefiting from properties, and in such a case lineage is not established even if he claims it. The third: semblance of right through a contract, so he thinks intercourse is lawful by it, even if that contract is void and invalid; like intercourse with a woman in her waiting period after three pronouncements or for a payment after marriage during the waiting period. And if you wish, for further detail on this noble topic, refer to my treatise: 'The Decisive Statement on the Dropping of the Penalty for Marrying Close Relatives'. His statement: 'separation'; by irrevocable divorce, whether three or less, or by khul', or otherwise. His statement: 'because he'; meaning that the divorcer acknowledged the lineage by his claim, and a person is held to his admission. His statement: 'by the minor approaching puberty' - with a kasra on the ha - it is said: the boy approaches puberty, so he is a minor approaching puberty, and the girl approaches puberty, so she is a minor approaching puberty: when she approaches puberty, having reached the age of puberty, but not having [yet] reached puberty. His statement: 'and above'; that is, more than nine to fifteen; because if she reaches fifteen and no signs of puberty appear in her, she is legally an adult; for the age of puberty for both man and woman is fifteen according to the correct view. His statement: 'minimum duration of pregnancy'; said the commentator al-Harawi: the lineage of a minor approaching puberty is established if her husband divorces her with an irrevocable or revocable divorce and she gives birth at less than nine months from the time of divorce, and she has not admitted the passing of the waiting period or has admitted it but not claimed pregnancy in it. Because she has come at a time that cannot be attributed to an event from outside; because the days of her waiting period by text are three months, so less than six months remain, so we attribute it to that the conception was either during the waiting period or during the marriage, even if the minor is not capable of producing semen, otherwise the lineage would be cut off from its origin. So it is attributed. And if she gives birth at nine months or more, lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; because the end of her waiting period has a specific basis, which is three months, and the characteristic of minority remains with certainty, which is incompatible with pregnancy due to her lack of fluid; so when six months have passed, the law has ruled the end of the waiting period, upon an event after it. Because there remains either six months or more, so it is possible that the conception was from someone other than the husband, causing doubt about his lineage, so it is neither established from the husband nor cut off from his origin; due to the possibility of marriage to another, then she gives birth from him at the minimum time of childbirth; due to the possibility of the other marriage and insemination together, and if more than six months remain, it is obvious. End. And in 'Tabyin al-Haqa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq by al-Zayla'i: This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and revocable and irrevocable are the same in this. And Abu Yusuf said: Lineage is established from him up to two years if it was irrevocable, and if it was revocable, it is established from him up to twenty-seven months, and after that it is not established. This is if she does not admit pregnancy nor the end of the waiting period. As for if she admits pregnancy, it is an admission from her of reaching puberty, so her statement is accepted, making her like an adult woman regarding the establishment of his lineage. And if she admits the end of the waiting period after three months, then gives birth to a child at less than six months from the time of admission and less than nine months from the time of divorce, his lineage is established due to the clear appearance of her lie. End.
Source pages p. 497

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the lineage of a child born to a divorced minor (مراهقة) who has not yet reached puberty. The matn states: 'A minor approaching puberty who gives birth at less than nine months [from divorce], and at nine months, no.' The sharh explains: If the child is born within less than nine months from the time of divorce (including both revocable and irrevocable), the lineage is established because the minimum pregnancy duration is six months and the iddah of a minor is three months (by Qur'an: 'three months' for those who do not menstruate). Thus, the total possible period for the child to be from the husband is nine months (6+3). If birth occurs at exactly nine months or more, lineage is not established according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad because after six months from divorce, the iddah is definitively over (as minor's iddah is three months, and she cannot menstruate), so the pregnancy must be from a subsequent relationship. The exception is if the husband claims the child (by دعوة) because his admission creates legal lineage. Abu Yusuf differs: in irrevocable divorce, lineage is established up to two years; in revocable, up to twenty-seven months, because he considers the possibility of extended pregnancy. The passage also covers cases where the woman admits pregnancy (which implies she has reached puberty, making her like an adult) or admits the waiting period ending but then gives birth prematurely, in which case lineage is established due to her contradictory admission. The legal reasoning is based on combining the minimum pregnancy term (6 months) and the iddah term (3 months) with the principle that doubt prevents establishing lineage. The relied-upon position for fatwa is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as stated in the text.

Key Terms
مراهقة (murāhiqah): A girl who has reached the age of 9 years or more but has not yet shown signs of puberty (menstruation).
عدة (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarrying.
شبهة (shubhah): A semblance of right or legal doubt that makes intercourse permissible in some respects, often used to avoid hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), if a divorced minor (murāhiqah) gives birth 10 months after the divorce, what is the ruling on the child's lineage?
A) Lineage is established because the pregnancy can last up to two years.
B) Lineage is established only if the husband claims the child.
C) Lineage is not established because the iddah ends after 3 months and the minimum pregnancy is 6 months, so 10 months is beyond the 9-month limit.
D) Lineage is established only if the divorce was revocable.

Key Takeaway
The lineage of a child born to a divorced minor is established only if born within 9 months of divorce; otherwise, it is not, unless the husband claims it, according to the majority of Hanafi scholars.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced

Establishing Lineage After Divorce: The Minor Divorcée and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the maximum period for establishing lineage after divorce for a minor and adult woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on when lineage is established for a minor divorcée, explain the reasoning behind each view, and identify the mufta bihi and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
For a minor, lineage is established only if birth occurs within nine months of divorce, due to certain timing of 'idda and minimum pregnancy.

When a divorced woman gives birth, the child's lineage to the ex-husband is not automatic. The Hanafi school carefully balances probability and certainty, particularly for a minor divorcée. This lesson unpacks an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold a strict nine-month limit, while Abu Yusuf allows up to two years. Understanding their arguments sharpens your ability to apply rules of evidence (shubha) in fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Question
What is the issue? When does the child of a divorcée belong to the ex-husband? The key variable is time since divorce.
For a minor, the 'idda is three months if consummated.
2
State the Zahir al-Riwayah Position
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold: if the child is born <9 months from divorce, lineage is established; if ≥9 months, it is not. Why 9 months? 3 months 'idda + 6 months minimum pregnancy.
This is based on certainty: the child must have been conceived during marriage or 'idda.
3
Examine the Opposing View
Abu Yusuf argues: lineage can be established up to 2 years (ba'in divorce) or 27 months (raj'i). He considers the possibility of intercourse even at the very end of the 'idda.
Abu Yusuf uses probability (shubha) more liberally.
4
Analyze the Reasoning (Talil)
The majority response: a minor lacks the capacity for pregnancy after divorce (no 'water'). Therefore, any birth after 9 months must be from another man. Durability of this lack of capacity is certain, so we do not indulge possibility.
The principle: lineage is established by shubha, not by shubha of shubha.
5
Determine the Practical Difference
Under the mufta bihi (Abu Hanifa/Muhammad), a child born 10 months after divorce is not attributed to the husband. Under Abu Yusuf, it would be (if within 2 years).
This affects inheritance, custody, and marriage restrictions.

Source Text

وهي لم تقر بمضي العدة أو أقرّت ولم تدع حبلاً فيها. لأنها قد جاءت لمدّة لا يمكن أن يحمل على أمر حادث من خارج ؛ لأنَّ أيام عدتها بالنص ثلاثة أشهر، فبقي أقل من ستة أشهر ، فحملناها على أنَّ العلوق إمّا أن يكون في العدة أو في النكاح ، وإن لم يكن الصغير من أهل الماء، وإلا لزم انقطاع النسب عن أصله. فيحمل ولو أتت به لتسعة أشهر فصاعداً لا يثبت النسب عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ؛ لأنَّ لانقضاء عدتها جهة معينة، وهو ثلاثة أشهر ، وصفة الصغر باقية باليقين، وهي منافية للحمل لعدم مائها ، فإذا مضت ستة أشهر فقد حكم الشرع بانقضاء العدة، على أمر حادث بعدها. لأنه بقي إما ستة أشهر أو أزيد فيحتمل أن يكون العلوق من غير الزوج، فيقع الشك في نسبه، فلا يثبت عن الزوج ولا ينقطع أيضاً عن أصله ؛ لاحتمال التزوج بالآخر، ثم ولدت منه لأقل زمان الولادة ؛ لاحتمال كون النكاح الآخر والإنزال معاً وإن بقي أكثر من ستة أشهر فظاهر». انتهى. وفي «تبيين الحقائق شرح كنز الدقائق للزيلعي هذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد ، والرجعي والبائن فيه سواء، وقال أبو يوسف الله : يثبت النسب منه إلى سنتين إذا كان بائناً، وإن كان رجعيّاً يثبت منه إلى سبعة وعشرين شهراً ، وبعده لا يثبت، وهذا إذا لم تقر بالحبل ولا بانقضاء العدة. وأما إذا أقرت بالحبل فهو إقرار منها بالبلوغ، فيقبل قولها، فصارت كالكبيرة في حق ثبوتِ نسبه، وإن أقرّت بانقضاء العدّة بعد ثلاثة أشهر، ثم جاءت بولد لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار، ولأقل من تسعة أشهر من وقت الطلاق، يثبت نسبه (1) لظهور كذبها بيقين». انتهى و في «فتح القدير» (۲) : حاصلُ المسألة : إنّ الصغيرة إذا طلقت فإما قبل الدخول أو بعده، وإنما اعتبر أقل مدة الحمل ،هاهنا وأكثر مدة الحمل في البالغة ؛ لأنَّ النَّسب يثبتُ بالشبهة لا بشبهة الشبهة. [٢] 6 ففي البالغة شبهة الوطء زمانُ النكاح أو العدة ثابتة، وحقيقة الوطء في أحد هذين الزمانين توجب ثبوت النسب ، فكذا شبهته بعيده، فإن كان قبله فجاءت بولد لأقل من ستة أشهر يثبت نسبه، للتيقن بقيامه قبل الطلاق، وإن جاءت لأكثر منها لا يثبت ؛ لأنَّ الفرضَ أن لا عدة عليها، ولا يلزم كونه قبل الطلاق، فتلزم العدة. ي وإن طلقها بعد الدخول، فإن أقرت بانقضاء العدّة بعد ثلاثة أشهر ثم ولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار ثبت وإن لستة أشهر أو أكثر لا يثبت؛ لانقضاء العدة بإقرارها ، ولا يستلزم كونه قبلها حتى يتيقن بكذبها. وإن لم تقر بانقضائها ولم تدع حبلا ، فعندهما إن جاءت به لأقل من تسعة أشهر من وقتِ الطلاق يثبت نسبه وإلا فلا ، وعند أبي يوسف له يثبت إلى سنتين في البائن، وإلى سبعة وعشرين شهرا في الرجعي ؛ لاحتمال وطئها في آخرِ عدّتها الثلاثة أشهر ، وإن ادعت حبلا فكالكبيرة. [١] قوله : وإنما اعتبر ... الخ ؛ بيان للفرق بين مسألة الصغيرة المطلقة حيث اعتبروا في باب ثبوتِ نسب ولدها الذي جاءت بعد الطلاق أقل مدة الحمل، حيث قالوا : إن جاءت به لأقل من تسعة أشهر من وقتِ الطلاق يثبت نسبه منه ؛ لتيقن كون العلوق في العدة أو في النكاح فإنّه إن كان علوقه بعد العدة وهو ثلاثة أشهر لزِمَ كون الجنين في بطن أمه أقل من ستة أشهر، ، وإن جاءت به لأكثر من تسعة أشهر أو لتسعة أشهر لا يثبت نسبه منه ؛ لعدم تيقن كون العلوق في العدة أو قبلها ؛ لأنَّ الباقي هاهنا بعد حذفِ العدة ستة أشهر أو أكثر، فيحتمل كون العلـوق بعد العدّة ، وبين مسألة الكبيرة المطلقة حيث اعتبروا هناك أكثر مدة الحمل، وقالوا : إن ولدت لأقل من سنتين يثبت نسبه وإلا لا، هذا في المبتوتة، وفي غيرها : يثبت نسبه لأكثر من سنتين ما لم تقر بانقضاء العدة. (٢) قوله : ففي البالغة... الخ ؛ الحاصل أن في المطلقة الكبيرة حقيقة الوطء في زمان النكاح أو العدّة تُثبت النسب ، فكذا توجيه شبهته ، فتعتبر شبهته احتياطاً، ويحكم
And she did not acknowledge the passing of the 'idda, or she acknowledged and did not claim pregnancy in it. Because she came with a period that cannot be attributed to an external event; because the days of her 'idda by text are three months, so less than six months remained, so we attribute it to the impregnation either being in the 'idda or in the marriage, even if the minor is not of the people of water, otherwise lineage would be cut off from its origin. So it is attributed. And if she brings him after nine months or more, lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; because the end of her 'idda has a specific way, which is three months, and the description of minority remains with certainty, and it is incompatible with pregnancy due to her lack of water. So when six months have passed, the law has ruled the completion of the 'idda, on an event after it. Because there remains either six months or more, so it is possible that the impregnation is from other than the husband, so doubt occurs about his lineage, so it is not established from the husband nor does it become severed from his origin; due to the possibility of marrying another and then giving birth from him in less than the minimum period of childbirth; due to the possibility of the other marriage and intercourse together, even if more than six months remain, it is apparent. End. And in Tabyin al-Haqa'iq Sharh Kanz al-Daqa'iq by al-Zayla'i: this is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and the raj'i and ba'in are the same in it. And Abu Yusuf said: lineage is established from him up to two years if it is ba'in, and if it is raj'i, it is established from him up to twenty-seven months, and after that it is not established. This is if she did not acknowledge pregnancy nor the completion of the 'idda. As for if she acknowledges pregnancy, that is an admission of her reaching puberty, so her statement is accepted, so she becomes like an adult regarding the establishment of his lineage. And if she acknowledges the completion of the 'idda after three months, then she brings a child in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment and less than nine months from the time of divorce, his lineage is established due to the clear appearance of her lie. End. And in Fath al-Qadir: The summary of the issue: The minor if divorced is either before consummation or after. And only the minimum period of pregnancy is considered here, and the maximum period of pregnancy in the adult; because lineage is established by probability, not by probability of probability. So in the adult, the probability of intercourse during the time of marriage or 'idda is established, and the reality of intercourse in one of these two times necessitates the establishment of lineage, so likewise its probability after it. Because if it is before it and she comes with a child in less than six months, his lineage is established, due to certainty of its existence before divorce. And if she comes with more than that, it is not established; because the assumption is that there is no 'idda upon her, and it is not necessary that it be before divorce, so 'idda becomes necessary. And if he divorces her after consummation, then if she acknowledges the completion of the 'idda after three months, then gives birth in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, it is established; but if six months or more, it is not established; due to the completion of the 'idda by her acknowledgment, and it does not necessitate being before it so that her lie is confirmed. And if she does not acknowledge its completion nor claim pregnancy, then according to both of them: if she brings him in less than nine months from the time of divorce, his lineage is established; otherwise no. And according to Abu Yusuf: it is established up to two years in ba'in, and up to twenty-seven months in raj'i; due to the possibility of intercourse in the last part of her three-month 'idda. And if she claims pregnancy, then it is like the adult. [1] His saying: 'And only the minimum period of pregnancy is considered...' etc.; an explanation of the difference between the case of the minor divorcée where they considered in the chapter of establishing the lineage of her child that she brings after divorce the minimum period of pregnancy, where they said: If she brings him in less than nine months from the time of divorce, his lineage is established from him; due to certainty that impregnation was during the 'idda or during the marriage; because if his impregnation was after the 'idda which is three months, it would necessitate the fetus being in his mother's womb for less than six months. And if she brings him after more than nine months or at nine months, his lineage is not established from him; due to lack of certainty that impregnation was during the 'idda or before it; because what remains here after subtracting the 'idda is six months or more, so it is possible that impregnation was after the 'idda. And between the case of the adult divorcée where they considered there the maximum period of pregnancy, and said: If she gives birth in less than two years, his lineage is established, otherwise no; this is in the irrevocable divorce; and in other than it, his lineage is established for more than two years as long as she does not acknowledge the completion of the 'idda. (2) His saying: 'So in the adult...' etc.; the summary is that in the adult divorcée, the reality of intercourse during the time of marriage or 'idda establishes lineage, so likewise its probability is directed, so its probability is considered as a precaution, and it is ruled.
Source pages p. 498

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school regarding the conditions for establishing lineage (thubut al-nasab) when a woman is divorced and later gives birth. The discussion distinguishes between a minor (saghira) and an adult (baligha) woman. The author first presents the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: for a minor divorcée, if she gives birth within less than nine months from the time of divorce, lineage is established. This is because the 'idda of a minor is three months if consummated, and the minimum period of pregnancy is six months. If the birth occurs after nine months or more, it is possible that the child was conceived after the 'idda, so lineage is not established. However, the child is not affiliated with anyone else either, pending possibility. Abu Yusuf differs: he allows lineage to be established up to two years for a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce and up to twenty-seven months for a raj'i (revocable) divorce. The reasoning is that the possibility of intercourse even at the end of the 'idda extends the window. The passage then explains the ruling for the adult woman, where the maximum period of pregnancy (two years according to Hanafi) is considered. The commentary clarifies that the reason for using the minimum period for the minor and the maximum for the adult is that lineage is established by strong probability (shubha) for the adult, but for the minor, only a certain probability (shubha of shubha) is insufficient. The text also covers special cases: if the woman admits pregnancy (which makes her like an adult) or admits completion of 'idda and then gives birth in less than six months, lineage is established due to clear contradiction. The overall ruling: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, for a minor divorcée who does not admit pregnancy or completion of 'idda, lineage is established only if the child is born less than nine months from divorce. For an adult, if she gives birth within two years from divorce (or more if she does not admit 'idda completion), lineage is established. Abu Yusuf's view is more expansive but is not the relied-upon position in the school.

Key Terms
صغيرة (saghira): A minor girl who has not reached puberty; in this context, she is divorced and may not have the capacity for pregnancy due to lack of 'water' (menstrual fluid).
عدة ('idda): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage. For a minor, it is three months (if consummated).
علوق ('uluq): The act of conception or impregnation; the moment the child is conceived.
شبهة (shubha): A strong probability or semblance that gives legal effect; here, the probability that intercourse occurred during marriage or 'idda.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, a minor divorcée gives birth 8 months after divorce. Is the child's lineage established?
A) Yes, because it's within 9 months.
B) No, because it's more than 6 months.
C) Yes, because it's less than 2 years.
D) No, because she is a minor.

Key Takeaway
For a minor divorcée, lineage is established only if the child is born within nine months of divorce, as per the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), ensuring certainty over probability.

Talaq — Divorce

Establishing Paternity for Divorced Adolescents: The Abu Hanifa–Abu Yusuf Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on paternity for adolescent divorcee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi positions on establishing paternity for a divorced adolescent girl (murahiqah) and identify the basis of the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Paternity for a divorced adolescent depends on the strength of shubha and attributing puberty to the nearest time.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah delves into the critical distinction between established paternity for a divorced minor and an adult woman, then presents the nuanced case of the adolescent girl who has not yet reached puberty. The commentary reveals a key intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad limit paternity to a short window based on the maxim that events are attributed to the nearest time, while Abu Yusuf extends the period based on the possibility of intercourse during the iddah. We will unpack this reasoning and its practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle of shubha
Identify that paternity is established by a 'semblance' (shubha) of legitimate intercourse, not by certainty. For minors, the semblance is too weak (shubhat al-shubha), while for adults it is strong enough to consider the maximum gestation period.
Shubha here means a legally plausible possibility, not mere doubt.
2
Distinguish minor vs adult rulings
For a divorced minor (saghirah), only the minimum gestation period (6 months) is considered; paternity is established if birth occurs within 9 months of divorce. For an adult (balighah), the maximum period (2 years) is considered because actual intercourse could have occurred during marriage or iddah.
The difference arises because pregnancy requires puberty, which a minor lacks.
3
Identify the adolescent dispute and its root
The adolescent (murahiqah) is between minor and adult – she has not reached puberty but is close. The key question: how to treat the possibility of intercourse during the iddah?
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad see puberty as a new event attributed to the nearest time.
4
Trace Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's reasoning
They apply the maxim: an unknown event (puberty) is attributed to the nearest possible time, i.e., six months before birth. Thus, if the child is conceived after puberty, it must be at least six months before birth. Since the adolescent had not yet reached puberty at divorce, effective intercourse could only have occurred after puberty – but the iddah is only three months. So the child must be born within six months of the nearest puberty time, effectively capping paternity to a short window after divorce.
This uses the minimum gestation period as a benchmark.
5
Trace Abu Yusuf's reasoning
Abu Yusuf counters that the possibility of intercourse during the revocable iddah (three months) is lawful, and the husband could have had intercourse at the very end of the iddah. Thus, the child could be born up to three months plus the maximum gestation (24 months) = 27 months. For an irrevocable divorce, he considers the possibility of pregnancy at the time of divorce or after iddah, similar to an adult woman, giving a 2-year window.
Abu Yusuf's view prioritizes the possibility of actual intercourse over the attribution of puberty.
6
Note the thamarah al-khilaf and practical impact
Under Abu Hanifa/Muhammad, paternity for an adolescent is almost never established if birth occurs more than a few months after divorce. Under Abu Yusuf, it can be established up to 27 months for revocable divorce. The mufta bihi in the school is the former, but Abu Yusuf's view is recognized.
This difference can affect inheritance, custody, and social status of the child.

[٣] قوله : وإن كان الطلاق بائنا ... الخ ؛ حاصله أنَّ عند أبي يوسف له : إن كان طلاق تلك المراهقة رجعيّاً يعتبر في ثبوتِ النسب سبعة وعشرون شهراً ؛ لأنه يمكن جعله واطناً في آخر عدتها - أي ثلاثة أشهر - ؛ لكون الوطء حلالاً في عدة الرجعي، ثم يحكم بأنها جاءت به لأكثر مدة الحمل، وهو أربعة وعشرون شهراً.
وإن كان الطلاق بائناً يعتبر في ثبوتِ النَّسب سنتان من وقت الطلاق ؛ لأنه يحتمل أن تكون حاملاً وقت الطلاق فيكون انقضاء عدتها بوضع الحمل، ويحتمل كونها حاملة بعد انقضاء العدّة بثلاثة أشهر، وإذا كان كذلك كانت كالبالغة إذا لم تقر بانقضاء العدة، حيث يثبت نسبها إلى سنتين.

Book of Divorce, Chapter on Establishing Paternity and Custody. Only the minimum period of pregnancy is considered here, and the maximum period of pregnancy for an adult woman; because paternity is established by a semblance (shubha), not by the semblance of a semblance. [2] 6 For an adult woman, the semblance of intercourse during the time of marriage or the waiting period is established, and actual intercourse in either of these two times necessitates establishing paternity, so likewise its semblance after it. If it was before it, and she gives birth to a child at less than six months, his paternity is established, due to certainty of its existence before the divorce. And if she gives birth at more than that, it is not established, because the assumption is that there is no waiting period upon her, and it is not necessary that it was before the divorce, so the waiting period is necessary. And if he divorced her after consummation, and she admitted the completion of the waiting period after three months, then gave birth at less than six months from the time of admission, it is established; but if at six months or more, it is not established, because the waiting period ended by her admission, and it does not necessitate that it was before it so that we become certain of her lying. And if she did not admit its completion and did not claim pregnancy, then according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) if she gives birth at less than nine months from the time of divorce, his paternity is established, otherwise not. And according to Abu Yusuf, it is established up to two years in irrevocable divorce, and up to twenty-seven months in revocable divorce, due to the possibility of intercourse at the end of her three-month waiting period. And if she claimed pregnancy, then it is like an adult woman. [1] His statement: 'Only the minimum...' etc., is an explanation of the difference between the case of the divorced minor girl where they considered in the chapter of establishing paternity of her child born after divorce the minimum period of pregnancy, as they said: if she gives birth at less than nine months from the time of divorce, his paternity is established from him, due to certainty of conception during the waiting period or during the marriage; for if conception was after the waiting period, which is three months, it would necessitate the fetus being in her womb less than six months. And if she gives birth at more than nine months or at nine months, his paternity is not established from him, due to lack of certainty that conception was during the waiting period or before it, because the remainder here after subtracting the waiting period is six months or more, so it is possible that conception was after the waiting period. And between the case of the divorced adult woman where they considered there the maximum period of pregnancy, and they said: if she gives birth at less than two years, his paternity is established, otherwise not. This is for the irrevocably divorced woman; for others, his paternity is established for more than two years as long as she does not admit the completion of the waiting period. (2) His statement: 'For the adult woman...' etc.; the summary is that for the divorced adult woman, actual intercourse during the time of marriage or the waiting period establishes paternity, so likewise directing its semblance, so its semblance is considered as a precaution, and it is judged... [1] 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. And as for the adolescent girl, the semblance of intercourse during marriage or during the waiting period, which is three months, is established. Then actual intercourse in either of these two times does not necessitate establishing paternity, due to the lack of attainment of puberty. So puberty, which is an event, is attributed to the nearest time, which is six months to the time of birth. This is the school of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. And according to Abu Yusuf, if the divorce was revocable, then up to twenty-seven months: her waiting period and two years the maximum period of pregnancy; and if the divorce was irrevocable, then up to two years. Because three months. Two years. Establishing paternity up to two years. [2] Contrary to the minor girl, for actual intercourse in her does not necessitate establishing paternity, because pregnancy is a characteristic of puberty, and there is no puberty here, so its semblance here descends to the semblance of a semblance, and what is considered in such matters is the semblance, not what is below it. [1] His statement: 'is attributed': because it is established that an event whose time of occurrence is unknown is attributed to the nearest time of its existence. And for this reason, it is mentioned in 'al-Ashbah' and elsewhere: if a man sees traces of semen on his garment after he prayed Fajr, Dhuhr, and others, and he did not recall having a wet dream, then he should perform ghusl and repeat the prayers that he prayed between the time of his discovery and the nearest sleep he slept. [2] His statement: 'up to seven': the apparent is that he should say: up to less than twenty-seven, because the part that completes the twenty-seventh month is outside this count. [3] His statement: 'And if the divorce was irrevocable...' etc.; its summary is that according to Abu Yusuf: if the divorce of that adolescent was revocable, twenty-seven months are considered in establishing paternity, because it is possible to consider him as having intercourse at the end of her waiting period, i.e., three months, because intercourse is lawful during the revocable waiting period, then it is judged that she gave birth at the maximum period of pregnancy, which is twenty-four months. And if the divorce was irrevocable, two years from the time of divorce are considered in establishing paternity, because it is possible that she was pregnant at the time of divorce, so her waiting period ends with delivery, and it is possible that she became pregnant after the completion of the waiting period of three months. And when this is the case, she is like an adult woman who did not admit the completion of the waiting period, where her paternity is established up to two years. (1) 'al-Ashbah (1:217).
Source pages p. 499

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) on a matn from the chapter on establishing paternity (thubut al-nasab) and custody (hadanah). The author explains the key distinction between the rules for a divorced minor girl (saghirah) and a divorced adult woman (balighah), and then presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a divorced adolescent girl (murahiqah). The central legal principle is that paternity is established by a 'shubha' (semblance of legitimate intercourse) rather than by certainty. For a minor girl who is divorced before consummation, the minimum period of pregnancy (six months) is considered because the possibility of pregnancy itself after divorce is weak. If she gives birth within nine months of divorce, paternity is established, as conception must have occurred during the marriage or iddah. For an adult woman, the maximum period of pregnancy (two years) is considered because actual intercourse could have occurred during the marriage or iddah. The text then discusses the case of a murahiqah (adolescent who has not yet reached puberty). Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad rule that for her, paternity is established only if she gives birth within six months of the nearest possible time of puberty (which they assume to be six months before birth). This is based on the maxim that a new event (like puberty) is attributed to the nearest possible time. Abu Yusuf disagrees: if the divorce is revocable (raj'i), he extends the period to twenty-seven months (three months of iddah plus two years), because the husband may have had intercourse at the end of the iddah. If the divorce is irrevocable (ba'in), he extends it to two years from the time of divorce, similar to the adult woman who does not admit the end of her iddah. The commentary also justifies the maxim of attributing events to the nearest time with an illustration from the book al-Ashbah about a man finding traces of semen.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A semblance or plausible basis for a legal ruling, here specifically the possibility that intercourse occurred during a valid marriage or iddah, sufficient to establish paternity.
شبهة الشبهة (shubhat al-shubha): A semblance of a semblance; an even weaker basis. For a minor girl, even if there was a semblance of intercourse, it is too weak to establish paternity because pregnancy requires puberty, which is absent.
علوق (alaq): Conception; the moment when pregnancy begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The principle that the maximum gestation period for a minor is six months
B) The maxim that an event is attributed to the nearest time, specifically puberty
C) The fact that an adolescent cannot conceive due to lack of puberty
D) The rule that all divorced women must wait until the end of iddah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that paternity for a divorced adolescent girl is established only if birth occurs within six months of the earliest possible puberty, though Abu Yusuf extends the period to up to two years based on the possibility of intercourse during iddah.

Lineage of a Murahaqah: The Nearest Possible Time Principle
Intra-Hanafi dispute on attributing lineage to nearest possible time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-school dispute on attributing lineage for a divorced murahaqah and apply the principle of aqrab al-awqat (nearest possible time) to determine the timeframe for paternity.

Core Idea
A murahaqah's unknown puberty is attributed to the nearest possible time – six months before birth – by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, but Abu Yusuf allows longer periods.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the confirmation of paternity (nasab) when a near-pubescent girl (murahaqah) is divorced and later gives birth. The key question is: to what point in time can the birth be attributed? The answer hinges on a fundamental Hanafi principle: an event of unknown origin is attached to the nearest possible time of its occurrence (aqrab al-awqat). The passage presents the positions of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani versus Abu Yusuf, and then expands on the principle with an analogy from impurity rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Legal Issue
The passage deals with a divorced murahaqah (near-pubescent girl) who gives birth. Actual intercourse during marriage or 'iddah does not automatically establish lineage because she has not reached puberty. The question is: how long after divorce can the birth be attributed to the ex-husband?
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute, so both positions are within the school.
2
State the Positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: lineage is established if the child is born within six months of divorce or end of 'iddah. Abu Yusuf: for revocable (raj'i) divorce, up to 27 months; for irrevocable (ba'in) divorce, up to 2 years.
The six-month period is derived from the minimum duration of pregnancy.
3
Analyse the Reasoning
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad apply the principle that an event of unknown time (here, the onset of puberty) is attributed to the nearest possible time. Since puberty must precede birth by at least six months (the minimum pregnancy), the birth is attributed to six months prior. Abu Yusuf considers the possibility that intercourse occurred during the 'iddah (raj'i) or before divorce (ba'in), allowing longer windows.
The commentary clarifies that for revocable divorce, intercourse is permissible during 'iddah, so up to 27 months (3 months 'iddah + 24 months max pregnancy).
4
Apply the Principle Elsewhere
The commentary provides an analogy: if a man sees semen on his garment after praying multiple prayers without recalling a wet dream, he must repeat the prayers from the time of the nearest sleep. This illustrates the same principle of attributing an unknown event to the nearest possible time.
This analogy strengthens the method of istidlal (reasoning) in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما في المراهقة فشبهة الوطء في النكاح، أو في العدة : وهي ثلاثة أشهر ثابتة ، ثُمَّ حقيقة الوطء في أحد هذين الزمانين لا يوجب ثبوت النسب ؛ لعدم تحقق البلوغ ، فالبلوغ وهو أمر حادث يضاف إلى أقرب الأوقات، وهو ستة أشهر إلى وقتِ الولادة، فهذا مذهب أبي حنيفة ومحمد . وأما عند أبي يوسف الله فإن كان الطلاق رجعيّاً، فإلى سبعة وعشرين شهراً ؛ مدة عدتها وسنتان أكثر مدة الحمل، وإن كان الطلاق بائنا"، فإلى لأن ثلاثة أشهر . سنتين بثبوت النسب إلى سنتين.
بخلاف الصغيرة، فإنّ حقيقة الوطء فيها لا توجب ثبوت النسب ؛ لكون الحمل من خواص البلوغ، ولا بلوغ هاهنا فشبهته ههنا تنزل إلى شبهة الشبهة، والمعتبر في أمثال هذا الباب هو الشبهة دون النازل عنها. ١ ] قوله : يضاف ؛ لما تقرّر أنَّ الحادث الذي لا يعلم زمان حدوثه يضاف إلى أقرب أوقات وجوده ، ولهذا ذكر في «الأشباه» (۱) وغيره : إنه لو رأى رجل أثر المني في ثوبه بعد ما صلى الصبح والظهر وغيرهما ولم يتذكر الاحتلام، فإنّه يغتسل ويعيدُ الصلوات التي صلاها بين وقت اطلاعِهِ وبين أقرب نومة نامها. [٢] قوله : فإلى سبعة ؛ الظاهر أن يقول : فإلى أقل من سبعة وعشرين ؛ لأنَّ الجزء الذي يتم به الشهر السابع والعشرون خارج من هذا المحسوب. [٣] قوله : وإن كان الطلاق بائنا ... الخ ؛ حاصله أنَّ عند أبي يوسف له : إن كان طلاق تلك المراهقة رجعيّاً يعتبر في ثبوتِ النسب سبعة وعشرون شهراً ؛ لأنه يمكن جعله واطناً في آخر عدتها - أي ثلاثة أشهر - ؛ لكون الوطء حلالاً في عدة الرجعي، ثم يحكم بأنها جاءت به لأكثر مدة الحمل، وهو أربعة وعشرون شهراً.
وإن كان الطلاق بائناً يعتبر في ثبوتِ النَّسب سنتان من وقت الطلاق ؛ لأنه يحتمل أن تكون حاملاً وقت الطلاق فيكون انقضاء عدتها بوضع الحمل، ويحتمل كونها حاملة بعد انقضاء العدّة بثلاثة أشهر، وإذا كان كذلك كانت كالبالغة إذا لم تقر بانقضاء العدة، حيث يثبت نسبها إلى سنتين.
As for the near-pubescent girl (murahaqah), there is a semblance (shubha) of intercourse during marriage or during the waiting period (‘iddah), which is three confirmed months. Then actual intercourse in either of these two times does not cause lineage to be established due to the lack of confirmed puberty. Puberty is a new occurrence attributed to the nearest possible time, which is six months before the time of birth. This is the doctrine of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. As for Abu Yusuf, may God have mercy on him: if the divorce was revocable (raj‘ī), then up to twenty-seven months — the duration of her ‘iddah and two years (the maximum duration of pregnancy). If the divorce was irrevocable (bā’in), then up to two years because of three months. (This is) regarding the establishment of lineage within two years. Unlike a minor girl, actual intercourse in her case does not cause lineage to be established because pregnancy is a characteristic of puberty, and there is no puberty here. So its semblance here descends to a semblance of a semblance, and what is considered in such cases is the higher semblance, not the lower. [1] His statement: 'is attributed' — because it is established that an event whose time of occurrence is unknown is attributed to the nearest possible time of its occurrence. For this reason, it is mentioned in al-Ashbāh and elsewhere: if a man sees traces of semen on his garment after having prayed Fajr, Zuhr, and other prayers without recalling a wet dream, then he must perform a ritual bath and repeat the prayers that he prayed between the time of his discovery and the nearest sleep he had. [2] His statement: 'to twenty-seven' — the apparent meaning is 'to less than twenty-seven months' because the part that completes the twenty-seventh month is excluded from this calculation. [3] His statement: 'if the divorce was irrevocable ... etc.' — its summary: according to Abu Yusuf, if the divorce of that near-pubescent girl was revocable, then in establishing lineage, twenty-seven months are considered because it is possible that he had intercourse at the end of her ‘iddah (i.e., three months), since intercourse is permissible during a revocable ‘iddah, and then it is ruled that she gave birth after the maximum duration of pregnancy (twenty-four months). If the divorce was irrevocable, then two years from the time of divorce are considered for establishing lineage because it is possible she was pregnant at the time of divorce, in which case her ‘iddah ends with delivery, and it is also possible she became pregnant after the end of the three-month ‘iddah. Being so, she is like an adult woman who does not acknowledge the expiry of her ‘iddah, where her lineage is established up to two years.
Source pages p. 500

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the confirmation of paternity (nasab) when a minor near-pubescent girl (murahaqah) is divorced and later gives birth. The issue arises because actual intercourse during the marriage or ‘iddah does not prove lineage in her case since she may not have reached puberty. However, since she is near puberty, there is a probability that she was pubescent at some point. The principle applied is that an event of unknown time (ḥādith) is attributed to the nearest possible time (aqrab al-awqāt). Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybānī hold that the birth is attributed to the six months prior to delivery (the minimum duration of pregnancy), so lineage is confirmed if the birth occurs at least six months after the divorce or the end of the ‘iddah. Abu Yūsuf distinguishes between revocable and irrevocable divorce. For a revocable divorce, he allows up to twenty-seven months (three months ‘iddah plus twenty-four months maximum pregnancy) because intercourse could have occurred at the end of the ‘iddah. For an irrevocable divorce, he allows two years from the time of divorce because it is possible she was already pregnant at divorce or became pregnant after the ‘iddah. The commentary then clarifies technical points: the attribution principle is supported by a similar ruling in al-Ashbāh about a man discovering semen on his garment; the twenty-seven months should be understood as less than twenty-seven; and the reason for the two-year limit for ba’in divorce is analogy with an adult woman who does not acknowledge the end of her ‘iddah.

Key Terms
المراهقة (al-murāhaqah): A female who has approached the age of puberty (bulūgh) but has not fully reached it, typically between the ages of nine and fifteen.
شبهة الوطء (shubhat al-waṭʾ): A legal semblance of intercourse that creates a possibility of paternity but does not constitute established actual intercourse.
أقرب الأوقات (aqrab al-awqāt): The nearest possible time to which an event of unknown origin is legally attributed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 6 months
B) 24 months
C) 27 months
D) 2 years

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school relies on the principle of aqrab al-awqat to attribute lineage of a murahaqah, with the mufta bihi being a six-month window, though Abu Yusuf allows longer periods for revocable and irrevocable divorces.

Lineage When Acknowledged Iddah Expiry Is Contradicted by Early Childbirth
Ruling on establishing lineage when acknowledgment of iddah expiry is contradicted by early childbirth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lineage when a woman acknowledges iddah expiry but gives birth within six months, and explain the reasoning based on certainty (yaqin).

Core Idea
If a woman gives birth within six months of acknowledging iddah expiry, her acknowledgment is false and lineage is established.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi family law: a woman in her waiting period ('iddah) claims that her 'iddah has ended, but then gives birth within six months of that claim. The Hanafi school uses the principle of certainty (yaqin) to override her own statement, establishing the child's lineage to the former husband. We will walk through the legal reasoning, the underlying proof, and the conditions under which lineage is or is not established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
First, identify the act under consideration: a woman in 'iddah acknowledges that her 'iddah has expired, then gives birth. The ruling is that the child's lineage is established to the ex-husband if the birth occurs within six months of the acknowledgment.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is a rational (aqli) argument based on the minimum duration of pregnancy (six months). The text states: 'the child does not remain in the womb less than six months.' This established fact serves as the basis for certainty.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
Since the minimum gestation is six months, a birth within six months of the acknowledgment proves that the woman was pregnant at the time of her claim. Therefore, her acknowledgment that the 'iddah had expired (which requires no pregnancy) is false with certainty.
4
Note the Qualifications and Ikhtilaf
If the birth occurs at six months or later, lineage is not established because the possibility exists that conception occurred after the 'iddah. The text also notes that if the acknowledgment was made long after the expiry (e.g., after a year), and the birth is less than six months from the acknowledgment but also less than two years from divorce, then falsehood is not certain. This ruling is the subject of valid scholarly disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعتدة أقرت بمضى العدة، وولدت لأقل من نصف سنة والجواب من قبلهما : إنّ لانقضاء عدتها جهة معينة وهو الأشهر ؛ لأنا عرفناها صغيرة بيقن، وما عرف كذلك لا يحكم بزواله بالاحتمال، فبمضي الأشهر يحكم الشرع بانقضاء عدتها ، فلا يعتبر خلافه المحتمل، بخلاف ما إذا ولدت لأقل من تسعة أشهر من وقت الطلاق. كذا في «الهداية» و«النهاية». (۱) قوله : ولم تقر...الخ ؛ قيّد به لكونه محل الخلاف، وأما إذا أقرت بانقضاء عدتها بثلاثة أشهر، فإن جاءت بولد لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار ثبت نسبه لظهور كذبها بيقين، وإن جاءت لستة أشهر أو أكثر من وقت الإقرار لا يثبت لانقضاء العدة بإقرارها ، ولا يتيقن حينئذ بكذب إقرارها. كذا في «الفتح» (۱) به [۲] قوله : ومعتدة ؛ بالجر، عطف على ما عطف عليه ما قبله والجملة المتصلة . صفة له؛ أي يثبت نسب ولد معتدة مقرّة بانقضاء عدتها إذا ولدت لأقل من ستة أشهرٍ من وقت الإقرار ؛ لأنه ظهر كذبه هاهنا بيقين ؛ إذ لا يبقى الولد في بطن أقل من ستَّةَ أشهر، فلما ولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار، عُلِمَ أنَّ الولد كان في بطنها عند الإقرار، فلغا إقرارها بانقضاء العدة، إذ لا تنقضي عدة الحامل إلا بوضع الحمل. وإن ولدت لستة أشهر فصاعداً من وقت الإقرار لا يثبت نسبه لعدم ظهور كذب إقرارها بيقين ؛ لاحتمال أن يكون العلوق بعد العدة، وهذا كله إذا أقرت بانقضاء العدة بأن قالت : انقضت عدتي في هذه الساعة، وإلا فيحتمل أن تقر بعد انقضائها بزمان طويل. كما إذا أقرّت بانقضائها بعد مضي سنة من وقت الطلاق، ثم ولدت لأقل من ستة أشهر من وقت الإقرار ولأقل من سنتين من وقتِ الفراق ، فإنّه يحتمل أن تكون عدتها انقضت في شهرين أو ثلاثة، ثمّ أقرّت بعد ذلك بزمان طويل ، فلا يظهر كذبها بيقين. كذا حققه في «البحر»(۲) وغيره.
And a woman in her waiting period (‘iddah) who acknowledged the passage of her ‘iddah, and then gave birth in less than six months [from that acknowledgment]. The response from both of them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the expiry of her ‘iddah has a specific aspect: the months, because we know with certainty that she was a minor, and what is known with certainty is not removed by mere probability. So with the passing of the months, the law (shar‘) judges that her ‘iddah has expired, and the contrary probability is not considered. Contrary to the case where she gives birth in less than nine months from the time of divorce. This is stated in al-Hidāyah and al-Nihāyah. [1] His statement: 'and did not acknowledge...' etc. — it is restricted because it is the subject of disagreement. As for if she acknowledges the expiry of her three-month ‘iddah, and then she produces a child in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, his lineage is established due to the manifest falsehood of her claim. If she produces a child after six months or more from the time of acknowledgment, lineage is not established due to the expiration of her ‘iddah by her own acknowledgment, and her falsehood is not certain. This is in al-Fatḥ. [2] His statement: 'and a woman in her ‘iddah' — in the genitive, conjoined to what was conjoined before, and the attached sentence is a description of it; meaning: the lineage of the child of a woman in her ‘iddah who acknowledges the expiry of her ‘iddah is established if she gives birth in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, because her falsehood becomes apparent here with certainty; since the child does not remain in the womb less than six months. So when she gives birth in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, it is known that the child was in her womb at the time of acknowledgment, so her acknowledgment of the expiry of her ‘iddah is invalidated, because the ‘iddah of a pregnant woman does not end except with delivery. If she gives birth at six months or more from the time of acknowledgment, his lineage is not established due to the lack of certain falsehood of her acknowledgment; because it is possible that conception occurred after the ‘iddah. This all applies if she acknowledged the expiry of the ‘iddah by saying: 'My ‘iddah has ended at this hour.' Otherwise, it is possible that she acknowledged after a long time had passed since its expiry. For example, if she acknowledged its expiry after a year had passed from the time of divorce, then gave birth in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment and less than two years from the time of separation, it is possible that her ‘iddah ended in two or three months, and then she acknowledged after a long time, so her falsehood is not certain. This is as verified in al-Baḥr and elsewhere.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (dalil) concerning a woman who acknowledges that her ‘iddah has expired but then gives birth within six months of that acknowledgment. The Hanafi position is that her acknowledgment is overridden because she gives birth before the minimum duration of pregnancy (six months) from the time of acknowledgment, proving that she was actually pregnant at the time of her claim. Since the ‘iddah of a pregnant woman ends only with delivery, her acknowledgment is false, and the child is attributed to the former husband. Conversely, if she gives birth at six months or more, the possibility exists that conception occurred after the ‘iddah, so lineage is not established. The text also introduces a qualification: if the acknowledgment was made long after the expiry (e.g., after a year), and she gives birth less than six months from the acknowledgment but also less than two years from the divorce, then her falsehood is not certain because the ‘iddah could have ended earlier. Thus, lineage is established only when her falsehood is absolutely certain, i.e., when the birth occurs within six months of a detailed acknowledgment of the exact moment of expiry.

Key Terms
أقرت بمضى العدة (aqarrat bi-maḍā al-‘iddah): She acknowledged that her waiting period has passed and thus she is free to remarry.
ظهور كذبها يقيناً (ẓuhūr kadhibihā yaqīnan): The manifest falsehood of her statement is certain, i.e., the birth within six months proves she was pregnant at the time of her claim.
علوق (‘ulūq): Conception; the moment when pregnancy begins.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman acknowledges that her ‘iddah has ended, then gives birth five months after that acknowledgment, what is the ruling on the child’s lineage?
A) Lineage is established to the ex-husband
B) Lineage is not established
C) It depends on whether the divorce was revocable or irrevocable
D) The mother’s acknowledgment is upheld and lineage is not established

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a woman's acknowledgment of iddah expiry is overridden by the certain evidence of early childbirth (within six months), ensuring that lineage is correctly assigned.

Paternity When 'Iddah Woman Acknowledges Expiry But Gives Birth Within Six Months
Ruling on paternity for a woman in 'iddah who acknowledges expiry but gives birth within six months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paternity when a woman in 'iddah acknowledges expiry but gives birth within six months, and explain the disagreement with the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Acknowledgment of 'iddah expiry is rebutted by birth within six months because minimum gestation is six months.

In this passage, we examine a delicate case where a woman's own statement conflicts with physical reality. The Hanafi school must decide: does her acknowledgment bind, or does the birth override it? The resolution hinges on the principle that certain knowledge (yaqin) is not overridden by mere possibility. The ruling also involves a disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and core ruling
The passage deals with a woman in 'iddah who states her 'iddah has ended, then gives birth. The core ruling: if birth occurs within six months of that statement, paternity is established. Understand the outcome first.
2
Understand the epistemological basis
The ruling is grounded in certain knowledge (yaqin) that a full-term human gestation cannot be less than six months. This certain knowledge overrides the woman's mere acknowledgment (which is zanni).
The Hanafi school gives priority to qati evidence over zanni claims.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) initially analogized this case to a minor girl who cannot be pregnant; for her, 'iddah expires by months conclusively. They argued similar logic should apply here. Understand their qiyas (analogy) and why it fails for a mature woman.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf where Abu Hanifa's view prevails.
4
Differentiate the time reference
The ruling uses the time from the acknowledgment, not from the divorce. Many students confuse this. The commentator corrects a textual error where 'divorce' was written instead of 'acknowledgment'. Learn to apply the correct timing.
If birth occurs exactly six months or more after acknowledgment, paternity is not established because her statement may be true.

(And a woman in 'iddah who acknowledged the expiry of the 'iddah, and gave birth in less than half a year. 0.1 And the answer from both of them [the Sahibayn]: Indeed, the expiry of her 'iddah has a specific means, which is the months; because we know her as a minor with certainty, and what is known as such is not judged to have ceased by probability. So by the passing of the months, the law judges the expiry of her 'iddah, so the contrary probability is not considered. Unlike if she gave birth in less than nine months from the time of divorce. Thus in al-Hidayah and al-Nihayah. (1) His statement: 'and she did not acknowledge...etc.'; he restricted it to being the place of disagreement. And if she acknowledged the expiry of her 'iddah by three months, then she brought a child in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, his paternity is established due to the clear falsity of her acknowledgment. If she brought a child at six months or more from the time of acknowledgment, paternity is not established because the 'iddah has expired by her acknowledgment, and then her acknowledgment is not certainly known to be false. Thus in al-Fath. [2] His statement: 'And a woman in 'iddah'; in the genitive, conjoined to what preceded it, and the connected clause is an adjective for it; meaning: the paternity of the child of a woman in 'iddah who acknowledges the expiry of her 'iddah is established if she gives birth in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, because her falsehood becomes manifest here with certainty, since the fetus does not remain in the womb for less than six months. When she gave birth in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment, it is known that the child was in her womb at the time of acknowledgment, so her acknowledgment of the expiry of the 'iddah is invalid, since the 'iddah of a pregnant woman does not end except by delivery. If she gives birth at six months or more from the time of acknowledgment, his paternity is not established because there is no clear falsity of her acknowledgment with certainty, due to the possibility that conception occurred after the 'iddah. All this applies if she acknowledged the expiry of the 'iddah by saying: 'My 'iddah has expired at this hour.' Otherwise, it is possible that she acknowledges after a long time after its expiry. As if she acknowledged its expiry after a year from the time of divorce, then gave birth in less than six months from the time of acknowledgment and less than two years from the time of separation, it is possible that her 'iddah had expired in two or three months, then she acknowledged after a long time, so her falsehood is not manifest with certainty. Thus verified in al-Bahr and others. [PAGE_502] 502 And at half of it, no, and a woman in 'iddah whose pregnancy appears. 'Umda al-Ri'aya 'ala Sharh al-Wiqaya. And at half of it, no) because when she gave birth in less than half a year from the time of acknowledgment, her falsehood became manifest with certainty, so her acknowledgment is nullified. But if she gave birth at half a year or more from the time of divorce, paternity is not established because we do not know the invalidity of the acknowledgment. Then the word 'woman in 'iddah' includes every woman in 'iddah. (And a woman in 'iddah whose pregnancy appears. (4) [1] His statement: 'And at half of it'; he did not mention the ruling if she gave birth at more than half a year, because its ruling is known from the ruling of half a year by primary inference. [2] His statement: 'from the time of divorce'; thus in many corrected copies, but the correct is in some copies: 'from the time of acknowledgment', in both places, and it agrees with the words of many authors of reliable books. Rather, it is required by the commentator's own reasoning, for if the birth occurs at half a year after the divorce, certainty of the falsity of the acknowledgment is also obtained, as in the case of less, because they share the cause of the manifest falsity with certainty, where she acknowledged while her womb was occupied with water. In short: obtaining certain knowledge of the falsity of her acknowledgment in the case of giving birth in less than half a year, and not obtaining it in the case of half or more, as the commentator mentioned, is not conceivable unless the period is considered from the time of acknowledgment, not from the time of divorce. Hence most good scholars judged that the word 'divorce' in place of 'acknowledgment' is a slip of the pen of the commentator or the copyists of the explanation. (3) His statement: 'includes every woman in 'iddah'; i.e. whether from death or revocable or irrevocable divorce, whether minor or major, by months or by menstruation. Some excepted the post-menopausal woman based on what Fakhr al-Islam and others mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir of considering two years for her. [4] His statement: 'And a woman in 'iddah...etc.'; this is an explanation of the conditions for establishing paternity after explaining the period in which paternity is established and the period in which it is not established. And apparently it is conjoined to what preceded, and the Harawi commentator and others stated it. So the meaning: and the paternity of the child of a woman in 'iddah whose pregnancy appears is not established... etc.
Source pages p. 501

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from Al-Wiqaya regarding paternity of a child born to a woman in 'iddah. The core ruling is: If a woman in 'iddah acknowledges that her 'iddah has expired, but then gives birth within less than six months from that acknowledgment, her acknowledgment is proven false because a human fetus cannot be born before six months of gestation. Therefore, paternity is established. If she gives birth at six months or later, paternity is not established, as her acknowledgment may be true and the child could be conceived after the 'iddah. The commentator also addresses an objection from the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) who analogized this case to a minor girl whose 'iddah expires by months despite being too young for pregnancy. The response clarifies that for a minor, the 'iddah expiry is determined by the specific passage of months, but here the woman is mature and pregnancy is possible, so the acknowledgment cannot be relied upon when proven false by birth within six months. The passage also discusses a nuance: if the woman gives birth exactly at six months or more after the divorce (not the acknowledgment), the ruling differs because the period from divorce may allow the possibility of conception after the 'iddah. The commentator corrects a common textual error where 'time of divorce' was mistakenly written for 'time of acknowledgment'. Finally, the ruling applies to all types of 'iddah (divorce or death) except possibly for post-menopausal women as some scholars noted.

Key Terms
عدة ('iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage.
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity, specifically here the legal father-child relationship established by marriage.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, though not explicitly named here, the reasoning of preferring the manifest falsity over general analogy is a type of istihsan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A woman in 'iddah acknowledges, 'My 'iddah has expired at this hour.' She gives birth 7 months after this acknowledgment. Is the child's paternity established to the husband?
A) Yes, because she acknowledged expiry.
B) No, because the birth is after six months from acknowledgment, so her acknowledgment may be true.
C) Yes, because birth is within nine months.
D) No, because she gave birth after six months from divorce.

Key Takeaway
Paternity is established if a woman in 'iddah gives birth within six months of acknowledging expiry, because her acknowledgment is manifestly false.

Conditions for Establishing Lineage of a Mu'taddah's Child
Explains conditions for proving paternity during 'iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three primary conditions for establishing the lineage of a child born to a woman in 'iddah and apply them to determine whether lineage is established in a given scenario.

Core Idea
Lineage from a mu'taddah requires manifest pregnancy, husband's acknowledgment, or formal proof; her mere claim is insufficient.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on when the paternity of a child born to a woman in her waiting period ('iddah) is legally established. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah clarifies the conditions that must be met, addressing common misconceptions about the woman's own declaration and the timing of birth. We will work through the proofs and exceptions to understand the precise legal framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Determine the basic principle: lineage is not automatically established by the woman's claim; specific evidence is required. Note the ruling when birth occurs less than half a year from her declaration.
The text uses the woman's declaration (iqrar) as a starting point.
2
Analyze the time condition and textual correction
Examine the contradictory statements about calculating the half-year period: from the time of divorce or from the time of declaration? Understand the commentator's reasoning that the correct basis is the declaration, not divorce.
This is an intra-Hanafi textual issue resolved by most scholars.
3
Enumerate the conditions for establishing lineage
List the three primary conditions from the passage: (1) manifest pregnancy before birth, (2) husband's acknowledgment, (3) formal proof of birth via testimony of two men or one man and two women. Note the special case of testimony without direct viewing.
Each condition is an independent basis for establishing lineage.
4
Apply the conditions to a scenario
Given a factual scenario, determine whether lineage is established by checking each condition. For example, if the husband acknowledges the child, lineage is established regardless of pregnancy signs.
Practice applying the rule to solidify understanding.

وحاصل الدفع : أنه يمكن ذلك بأن دخلت امرأة بيتاً وقد علما قبل ذلك علم اليقين بأنه ليس في البيت أحد من النساء والرجال ولا حيوان ولا شيء، وجلسا على الباب، وليس لذلك البيت إلا باب واحد، فعلما الولادة برؤية الولد، أو سماع صوت بكائه، فحينئذ يحلّ لهما أن يشهدا بولادتها ، وذلك لأن الشهادة لا تنحصر في المشاهدة بل اليقين بأمر ، ولو بغيرها يكفي لأدائها وقبولها.

And for half of it, no. And a woman in 'iddah whose pregnancy is apparent. 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah 'ala Sharh al-Wiqayah. 'And for half of it, no' because when she gives birth in less than half a year from the time of declaration, her falsehood becomes certain, so her declaration is invalid. But if she gives birth at half a year or more from the time of divorce, lineage is not established because we do not know the falsity of the declaration. Then the term 'mu'taddah' includes every woman in 'iddah. 'And a woman in 'iddah whose pregnancy is apparent.' [1] His statement: 'and for half of it' – he did not mention the ruling when she gives birth after more than half a year because its ruling is known from the ruling of half a year by first priority. [2] His statement: 'from the time of divorce' – this is found in many corrected copies, but the correct version is in some copies: 'from the time of declaration' in both places, and this agrees with the speech of many authors of reliable books; indeed, it is required by the commentator's own reasoning, because if the birth occurs at half a year after divorce, certainty of the falsity of the declaration is also obtained, as in the case of less, due to the common cause of the certainty of her falsehood, since she declared while her womb was occupied with water. In summary: obtaining certain knowledge of the falsity of her declaration in the case of birth at less than half a year, and not obtaining it in the case of half or more, as the commentator mentioned, cannot be imagined unless the period is considered from the time of declaration, not from the time of divorce. From here, most scholars ruled that the word 'divorce' in place of 'declaration' is a slip of the commentator's pen or of the scribes of the commentary. [3] His statement: 'includes every woman in 'iddah' – meaning whether from death or revocable or irrevocable divorce, whether minor or major, by months or by menstruation, and some excepted the post-menopausal woman based on what Fakhr al-Islam and others mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding considering two years for her. [4] His statement: 'and a woman in 'iddah... etc.' – this is an explanation of the conditions for establishing lineage after explaining the period in which lineage is established and the period in which it is not. It is apparent that it is coordinated with what preceded it, and the Harawi commentator and others stated it. So the meaning: 'And the lineage of a child of a woman in 'iddah whose pregnancy is apparent is not established... etc.' (1) This is supported by the wording of al-Tanwir (625) and al-Kanz (p. 64) and others, and Mulla Khusraw in Durar al-Hukkam (1:407) attributed what occurred in Sharh al-Wiqayah to the scribe's oversight. Page 503: 'Or the husband acknowledged it, or her birth was established by complete evidence' – meaning the lineage of a child of a woman in 'iddah is established if she claims the birth and the husband denies it, and before the birth there was a manifest pregnancy, or the husband acknowledged the pregnancy, or two men or one man and two women testified to the birth, such that the woman entered a house... In summary: lineage is established when one of these conditions exists: manifest pregnancy, or the husband's acknowledgment of it, or establishment of birth by complete evidence, or the birth occurring within less than two years, or the acknowledgment of the heirs, or the woman who brought the child being a wife. Details of all that will follow. (1) And the general term 'mu'taddah' includes the woman in 'iddah from death and from irrevocable or revocable divorce, as stated by Fakhr al-Islam, Qadikhan, and other commentators of al-Jami' al-Saghir. Al-Sarakhsi restricted it to the irrevocable case. He said in al-Bahr: 'The truth is that in the revocable case, if she brings the child after more than two years, testimony is needed like the irrevocable case; otherwise, if less, his lineage is established by the testimony of the midwife by agreement, due to the existence of the marriage bed.' [1] His statement: 'pregnancy' – its manifestation is that signs of pregnancy exist such that they create a dominant probability that she is pregnant for everyone who sees her. Thus in al-Nahr, and in al-Siraj: its manifestation is that she brings the child in less than six months. [2] His statement: 'she entered a house... etc.' – this depiction is needed to rebut what is said: how can birth be established by complete evidence, i.e., testimony of two men or one man and two women, because knowledge of it is only obtained by being present at the place of birth and looking at the private parts, which is forbidden for men; if they do that, they become sinners so their testimony is not accepted, so testimony in this chapter is only conceivable from women. The gist of the rebuttal is that it is possible if a woman enters a house while the witnesses knew with certainty before that there is no woman, man, animal, or anything in the house, and they sit at the door, and that house has only one door; then they know the birth by seeing the child or hearing its crying. Then it is permissible for them to testify to her birth, because testimony is not confined to direct observation; rather, certainty of a matter, even by other means, is sufficient for its performance and acceptance. (1) al-Nahr al-Fa'iq (2:496).
Source pages p. 502

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is a commentary on Sharh al-Wiqayah, addressing the chapter on establishing lineage (nasab) and custody. It explains the conditions under which the paternity of a child born to a woman in 'iddah is proven. The text begins with a ruling: if a woman gives birth less than half a year from her declaration (iqrar) that she is pregnant, her claim is proven false with certainty, so lineage is not established. However, if she gives birth at exactly half a year or more from the time of divorce, we cannot be certain of her falsehood, yet lineage is still not established according to the author. The commentator notes a textual discrepancy: some copies say 'from the time of divorce' but the correct reading is 'from the time of declaration' because only then does the reasoning hold—if the birth occurs at half a year after divorce, the period could be shorter from declaration, making her falsehood certain. Most scholars consider the word 'divorce' a scribal error. The term 'mu'taddah' (woman in 'iddah) includes all types: from death, revocable or irrevocable divorce, young or old, whether her 'iddah is by months or by menstruation. Some exclude the post-menopausal woman based on a two-year waiting period mentioned by Fakhr al-Islam. The passage then lists the conditions for establishing lineage: manifest pregnancy (zahr al-habl), the husband's acknowledgment (iqrar al-zawj), or proof of birth by complete evidence (hujjah tammah), meaning testimony of two men or one man and two women. The commentator explains how men can testify without viewing the private parts: if witnesses know with certainty that a woman entered a house empty of others, then hear a child's cry or see the child, they can testify to the birth. Testimony does not require direct observation; certainty suffices. Other conditions mentioned briefly include birth within two years, acknowledgment of heirs, or the woman being a wife (mankuhah). The final part restricts the generality: in revocable divorce, if the child comes after two years, testimony is needed; otherwise, the midwife's testimony suffices due to the marriage bed (firash).

Key Terms
معتدة (mu'taddah): A woman who is in the waiting period ('iddah) following divorce or death of her husband. The text clarifies it includes all types: from death, revocable or irrevocable divorce, regardless of age or method of counting 'iddah.
ظهر حبلها (zahara habluha): When the signs of pregnancy become visible to others, creating a dominant probability that she is pregnant. The text mentions two definitions: presence of pregnancy signs that cause anyone seeing her to assume pregnancy, or that she gives birth in less than six months.
إقرار (iqrar): Acknowledgment or confession. In this context, the woman's declaration that the child is from her husband during 'iddah, or the husband's acknowledgment of the pregnancy or paternity.
حجة تامة (hujjah tammah): Complete evidence sufficient to prove a fact in court. Here it refers specifically to testimony of two men or one man and two women witnessing the birth, albeit without directly seeing the delivery itself, as explained by the commentator.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for establishing the lineage of a child born to a woman in 'iddah?
A) Manifest pregnancy before the birth.
B) The husband's acknowledgment of the child.
C) The woman's own declaration of pregnancy.
D) Formal testimony of two men or one man and two women.

Key Takeaway
Lineage from a mu'taddah is established only through objective evidence: manifest pregnancy, husband's acknowledgment, or formal testimony; the woman's own claim is insufficient.
