Establishing Lineage During 'Iddah: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on evidence required to prove lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa requires complete evidence (two men or one man and two women) to establish lineage of a child born during 'iddah, and distinguish this from the Sahibayn's position that one woman's testimony suffices.

Core Idea
If the 'iddah ends with delivery, there is no longer a marital bed — lineage must be proven anew with complete evidence.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The question: What evidence is needed to establish that a child born during the 'iddah period belongs to the former husband? The answer determines how easily lineage is proven in court.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the contested point
What is being disputed? Not the birth itself, but the evidentiary standard for proving that the child is from the former husband.
The dispute is about the number and gender of witnesses required.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and its exceptions
Abu Hanifa requires complete evidence (two men or one man and two women) unless there is a visible pregnancy or the husband confessed to the pregnancy. In those two cases, no witnesses are needed.
The exceptions rely on the fact that lineage was already established before birth.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that one woman's testimony suffices in all cases because the 'iddah itself creates a marital bed (firash) that obligates lineage; only the identification of the child is needed.
They analogize to the situation during an ongoing marriage.
4
Trace the Hanafi rebuttal
Abu Hanifa responds that the 'iddah ends with the woman's admission of delivery. Once the 'iddah is over, there is no longer an ongoing firash, so lineage must be proven from scratch, hence the need for complete evidence.
This rebuttal is based on the principle that a terminated legal status cannot serve as a basis for a new claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فالحاصل أن عند أبي حنيفة إن كان للمعتدة حبل ظاهر. والرجُلان على الباب حتى ولدت فعلم الولادة برؤية الولد، أو سماع صوته، وإنما قيد الحجة بالثامة حتى لا يثبت بشهادة امرأة واحدة على الولادة خلافاً لهما. والحاصل: إن شهادة النساء لا تكون حجة في تعيين الولد إلا إذا تأيدت بمؤيد من ظهور حبل أو اعتراف منه به، أو فراش قائم، وأما نفس الولادة فلا تثبت إلا بأحد من الأمور المذكورة عنده. [٣] قوله: فالحاصل...الخ؛ قال في «الهداية»: «إذا ولدت المعتدة ولداً لم يثبت نسبه عند أبي حنيفة له إلا أن يشهد بولادتها رجلان أو رجل وامرأتان إلا أن يكون هناك حبل ظاهر أو اعتراف من قبل الزوج، فيثبت النسب من غير شهادة. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد: يثبت في الجميع بشهادة امرأة واحدة؛ لأن الفراش قائم بقيام العدة، وهو ملزم للنسب، والحاجة إلى تعيين الولد أنه منها، فيتعين بشهادتها كما في حال قيام النكاح. ولأبي حنيفة: إن العدة تنقضي بإقرارها وضع الحمل، والمنقضي ليس بحجة، فمسّت الحاجة إلى إثبات النسب ابتداءً، فيشترط كمال الحجة، بخلاف ما إذا كان ظهر الحبل أو صدر الاعتراف من الزوج؛ لأن النسب ثابت قبل الولادة، والتعيين يثبت بشهادتها». انتهى
So the conclusion: according to Abu Hanifa, if the woman in 'iddah has a visible pregnancy... the two men were at the door until she gave birth and they learned of the birth by seeing the child or hearing its cry. He only qualified the evidence as complete so that it is not established by the testimony of one woman regarding the birth, contrary to them. The summary: The testimony of women is not proof in identifying the child unless it is supported by a supporter of visible pregnancy, or his confession to it, or an existing marital bed. As for the birth itself, it is not established except by one of the mentioned matters according to him. [3] His statement: so the conclusion... etc.; He said in al-Hidayah: 'When a woman in 'iddah gives birth, her child's lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa unless two men or one man and two women testify to her giving birth, unless there is visible pregnancy or confession from the husband, then the lineage is established without testimony. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is established in all cases by the testimony of one woman because the marital bed is established by the existence of the 'iddah, and it necessitates lineage, and the need is to identify the child as hers, so it is identified by her testimony as in the case of an existing marriage. For Abu Hanifa: The 'iddah ends by her admission of having placed the pregnancy, and that which has ended is not evidence, so the need arises to establish the lineage anew, so complete evidence is required, contrary to when the pregnancy appeared or confession was issued from the husband, because the lineage was established before birth, and identification is established by her testimony.' End.
Source pages p. 504

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding the evidence required to establish the lineage of a child born to a woman during her 'iddah (waiting period) after divorce or death. The core issue is whether the testimony of a single woman (like a midwife) suffices to prove both the birth and the child's identity for lineage purposes. Abu Hanifa holds that lineage is not established unless there is complete evidence—two men or one man and two women—unless there is a visible pregnancy or the husband has confessed to the pregnancy. In those two cases, lineage is established even without testimony because the pregnancy or confession already proves the lineage before birth; the woman's testimony only identifies which child was born. The Sahibayn argue that the 'iddah itself creates an ongoing marital bed (firash), which obligates lineage, so the testimony of one woman is sufficient, similar to during an existing marriage. Abu Hanifa's reasoning is that the 'iddah ends with the woman's admission of delivery; after it ends, there is no longer an unbroken marital bed to rely on, so lineage must be proven from scratch with complete evidence. The text emphasizes that the term 'complete evidence' was specifically used to exclude the sufficiency of one woman's testimony, contradicting the Sahibayn. The practical consequence: in a court, under Abu Hanifa's view, a single female witness does not suffice to establish lineage unless supported by visible pregnancy or husband's confession; under the Sahibayn, it would suffice.

Key Terms
الحجة التامة (al-hujja al-tāmma): Complete evidence: testimony of two men or one man and two women.
الفراش (al-firāsh): The marital bed; the legal presumption of paternity based on a valid marriage or 'iddah.
المعتدة (al-muʿtadda): A woman in her waiting period ('iddah) after divorce or death of husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when does a woman's single testimony suffice to identify the child for lineage?
A) In all cases during 'iddah
B) Only when there is a visible pregnancy or the husband confessed to the pregnancy
C) Only when the husband is deceased
D) Never

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, establishing lineage after 'iddah requires complete evidence unless lineage was already proven before birth.

Establishing Lineage of a Widow's Child Within Two Years
Commentary on lineage establishment with proofs and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a widow's child's lineage is established without complete proof and explain the exception for minor widows.

Core Idea
Lineage is established for a widow's child born within two years if heirs affirm, but for minors it is only ten months and ten days.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the chapter of lineage and custody clarifies when a child born to a widow is automatically linked to the deceased husband. The general rule uses a two-year maximum pregnancy period, but a special rule applies for minor widows due to the presumption of non-pregnancy before puberty. You will learn the evidentiary requirements and a key intra-madhhab difference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its conditions
The text states that if a widow in her death-waiting period gives birth within two years of the husband's death and the heirs affirm the birth, the child's lineage is established without complete proof (hujjah tammah).
This applies even if pregnancy was not apparent and the husband did not acknowledge.
2
Distinguish birth from identification
The birth itself is proven by apparent pregnancy or the husband's acknowledgment; the testimony of one woman only serves to identify the child when there is a dispute.
The commentator clarifies a common confusion: the one-woman testimony does not establish the birth, only the identity of the newborn.
3
Recognize the exception for minor widows
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, if the widow is a minor (before puberty), lineage is established only if the birth occurs within ten months and ten days of death, because pregnancy is not presumed before puberty.
Abu Yusuf disagreed, holding that the two-year period applies even to minors.
4
Note Zufar's opinion and the Hanafi response
Zufar argued that if the child is born after the waiting period (four months ten days) by six months, lineage is not established. The Hanafis respond that the waiting period can also end by delivery, unlike a minor where pregnancy is improbable.
This reinforces the principle that the birth itself can extend the iddah.

[1] His statement: 'the birth is established ...' etc.; there is apparent leniency in it, for the establishment of birth in these two cases is not by the testimony of one woman, but rather by the appearance of pregnancy or his acknowledgment; rather, the testimony of one woman is needed only for the identification of the child when a dispute arises about it. How could it be otherwise when it is stated in al-Idah and al-Nihayah and others: that if divorce is suspended on her giving birth, it occurs according to him by the statement of the woman in her waiting period that she gave birth, because of his acknowledgment of the pregnancy or its appearance. [2] His statement: 'is established' means the birth itself, and likewise the identification. [3] His statement: 'in less than...' etc.; means the woman in death-waiting period gave birth in less than two years from the time of death, and the heirs of the deceased husband affirmed her giving birth, then the lineage of the newborn from the deceased is established without the need for complete proof, even if pregnancy was not apparent and the deceased's acknowledgment does not exist. [4] His statement: 'and it is established'; al-Ayni said in al-Binayah: 'This applies if the widow is not a minor; because the lineage of her child is established if she gives birth in less than ten months and ten days, and if she gives birth to more than that, it is not established according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, contrary to Abu Yusuf.' End. [1] His statement: 'and between two years'; up to here ends the expression of al-Bidayah, the text of al-Hidayah, and he said in al-Hidayah after it: 'Zufar said: If she brings the child after the completion of the death-waiting period by six months, the lineage is not established; because the law ruled the completion of her waiting period by months, due to the determination of the period, so it becomes as if she acknowledged the completion, as we explained in the case of a minor. But we say: her waiting period is completed by another means, which is the delivery of the pregnancy, contrary to the minor; because the default in her case is the absence of pregnancy, since she is not a suitable vessel before puberty, and there is doubt.' End. [2] His statement: 'so the child...' etc.; is a rebuttal to what is said: that 'child' is not derived, so that it could operate on the adverbial phrase, and his statement 'what is between...' is an adverbial for it. The gist of the rebuttal: that 'child' contains the meaning of a derived word, for it means 'the one born', and the definite article entering upon it is relative, so the meaning becomes: The lineage of the child of the widow who is born in a time between the death of the husband and the completion of two years is established. [3] His statement: 'at a time'; he indicated by it that what is meant by his statement 'what is between death and two years' is time. [4] His statement: 'then he mentioned'; meaning the author of al-Hidayah, and he indicated by 'then' a delay, for he mentioned in al-Hidayah after that issue the issue of the widow giving birth after acknowledging the completion of the waiting period, and after that he mentioned the issue of establishing lineage by complete proof and other things, along with what is in it of disagreement as we have transmitted previously, and after that he mentioned this issue as the commentator transmitted. [0] His statement: 'so he is his son'; he added after it: 'according to all of them', and with it the expression of al-Hidayah is completed.
Source pages p. 505

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah on the chapter of establishing lineage and custody in the book of divorce. It discusses the conditions under which the lineage of a child born to a widow is established. The main ruling is that if a widow gives birth within two years of her husband's death, and the heirs affirm the birth, the child's lineage is established without the need for complete proof (hujjah tammah) even if pregnancy was not apparent or the husband did not acknowledge it. This is because the two-year period is the maximum term of pregnancy according to the Hanafis. The commentator clarifies a point: the statement in al-Wiqayah uses 'and' (waw) for the heirs' affirmation, while al-Hidayah implies 'or' (aw), but the meaning is consistent. The text also addresses a subtlety: the testimony of one woman is sufficient for the identification of the child when there is a dispute, but the birth itself is established by the appearance of pregnancy or the husband's acknowledgment. Regarding a minor widow, al-Ayni in al-Binayah explains that if she is a minor (not having reached puberty), the lineage is established only if the birth occurs within ten months and ten days of the husband's death, according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani; Abu Yusuf differs. Zufar's opinion is also mentioned: if the child is born after the completion of the waiting period (four months and ten days) by six months, lineage is not established. The Hanafi response is that the waiting period can be completed by delivery, unlike a minor where pregnancy is not presumed. Finally, the commentator provides a grammatical analysis to defend the phrase 'what is between death and two years' as an adverbial phrase for the child meaning 'the one born'.

Key Terms
حجة تامة (hujjah tammah): Complete proof required to establish a child's lineage when there is no apparent pregnancy or acknowledgment by the husband; typically requires testimony of two men or one man and two women
عدة وفاة (iddat wafat): The waiting period for a widow, which is four months and ten days unless she is pregnant, in which case it lasts until delivery
صغيرة (saghirah): A minor female who has not reached puberty; in this context, a widow who is a minor

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition can the lineage of a child born to an adult widow be established without complete proof (hujjah tammah), according to the Hanafi school?
A) If the birth occurs within four months and ten days of the husband's death
B) If the birth occurs within two years of the husband's death and the heirs affirm it
C) If the widow is a minor and gives birth within ten months and ten days
D) If the husband acknowledged the child before death

Key Takeaway
The lineage of a widow's child is established without complete proof if the birth occurs within two years and the heirs affirm, but for minor widows the window is only ten months and ten days.

Critiquing the Interpretation of Conditions for Paternity in Iddah – The Five Objections to al-'Isam
Critical analysis of earlier commentary on paternity for mu'taddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five objections raised by the commentator against al-'Isam's reading of the conditions for paternity establishment for a mu'taddah, and explain the correct Hanafi position from al-Hidayah regarding the methods of proof.

Core Idea
The term 'mu'taddah' in paternity cases must distinguish between divorce and death iddah; using 'istikhdam' to merge them is contextually invalid.

This passage is a critical refinement from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya', where the author dissects an earlier commentary by al-'Isam on al-Wiqaya. The core dispute is about the correct referent of 'mu'taddah' in a sentence about paternity conditions. Al-'Isam attempted to apply the rhetorical device of istikhdam (using one word in two senses) to make the term cover both divorce and death iddah. The author argues that this interpretation is forced and contradicts the context, which clearly involves a husband's denial of birth—impossible in the case of death. Understanding this critique sharpens our ability to interpret legal texts accurately, especially regarding the distinct rules for iddah after divorce vs. death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ambiguous phrase
Locate the key sentence in al-'Isam's commentary: the mu'taddah who gives birth... if he denies... The ambiguity lies in whether 'mu'taddah' refers to divorced women only or includes widows.
The word 'mu'taddah' is the subject of a conditional clause that later mentions 'he denies' referring to a husband.
2
Consider the two possible meanings
Interpretation A: mu'taddah from divorce only. Interpretation B: general including death iddah. Evaluate each against the rest of the statement.
The text later adds conditions about heirs' acknowledgment and maximum pregnancy period of two years.
3
Test interpretation A with context
If mu'taddah is only from divorce, then phrases like 'heirs acknowledge' and 'less than two years' do not apply to divorce iddah but to death iddah, creating inconsistency.
Al-'Isam tries to resolve this by claiming the pronoun 'she gave birth' refers to death iddah while 'mu'taddah' refers to divorce iddah—this is the istikhdam device.
4
Analyze the author's five objections
The author lists five flaws: (1) the interpretation is forced and unnatural; (2) the specification of 'mu'taddah' to divorce lacks a mukhassis; (3) the later pronoun 'he denies' cannot refer to a deceased husband; (4) the denial is of the birth itself, not identification; (5) the interpretation contradicts the source text from al-Hidayah.
Each objection undermines the validity of al-'Isam's istikhdam.
5
Extract the correct Hanafi position
From al-Hidayah, the conditions differ: for mu'taddah from divorce (revocable or irrevocable), paternity is proven by testimony (two witnesses according to Abu Hanifa, one woman according to Sahibayn), appearance of pregnancy, or husband's acknowledgment. For mu'taddah from death, an additional method is heirs' acknowledgment.
The intra-Hanafi dispute on number of witnesses is a separate issue.

Source Text

والمنكوحة التي أتت به لستة أشهر ؛ أي التي هي غير مطلقة بل نكاحها قائم، فإن جحد ولادتها لهذا المولود يثبت تعينها بشهادة امرأة واحدة من غير اشتراط هذه الصفات». انتهى. أقول : قد سكت أكثر الناظرين في هذا المقام عن الحل والتنقيح، ولم يأتوا بما يفيد التوضيح، والعصام وإن أتى بما خلت عنه أكثر الحواشي، لكنّه لم يعصم عن زلّة الأقدام، فإن كلامه مخدوش عندي بوجوه :
أحدها : إنّ فيما اختاره تكلّفاً واضحاً يأبى . عنه السياق والسباق.
وثانيها : إنّ المراد بلفظ المعتدة الذي جعله مبتدأ لا يخلو إما أن يكون المراد به معتدة الطلاق فقط أو أعم منها ومن معتدة الوفاة، فإن أريد الأول فمع قطع النظر عن كون هذا التخصيص بلا مخصص لا يصح قوله : أو ولدت لأقل من سنتين وأقر الورثة بها ؛ لأنّ هذه المدة إنما تعتبر في المتوفى عنها زوجها لا في المطلقة، فإن في معتدة الرجعي يثبت النسب وإن جاءت به لأكثر من سنتين ما لم تقرّ بانقضاء العدة، وفي المبتوتة يثبت وإن جاءت لتمام سنتين على ما مر تفصيله.
وأيضاً لا يصح قوله : وأقرّ الورثة، فإنّ إقرار الورثة إنما يحتاج إليه في معتدة الوفاة، وأين الورثة من حياة الزوج.
فإن قلت : المراد بالمعتدة في ذلك القول هو معتدّة الطلاق، والمراد بضمير ولدت : معتدة الوفاة، بطريق صنعة الاستخدام.
قلت : هذا مع كونه لا يتبادر الفهم إليه يبطلُ بما يبطل به الشق الثاني ؛ أي المدة الأعم من لفظ المعتدة، وهو إن قوله الآتي : فإن جحد ولادتها، ضمير الجحود فيه راجع إلى الزوج، بقرينة قوله بعده، فيلا عن إن نفاه [؟]، وبشهادة قوله السابق : أقرّ به الزوج أو سكت.
وثالثها: إنه ظاهر كلامه الآتي سياقاً وسباقاً كما بيناه آنفاً يشهد بأن قوله : فإن جحد ... ... الخ بيان لإنكار الزوج، ولا يتصوّر هذا في صورة وفاته، فلا يرتبط الخبر بالمبتدأ.
ورابعها : إن قوله : فإن جحد ولادتها صريح في أنَّ الغرض منه إنكار نفس الولادة لا إنكار التعيين، فحمله عليه تعسّف أي تعسف والحق أن قوله : فإن جحد متعلق بقوله : منكوحة لا غير، كما ستطلع عليه عن قريب إن شاء الله.
وخامسها : إنّ «الوقاية» لما كانت ملخّصة ومأخوذة من «الهداية» لا بد أن يجعل تلخيصه موافقاً لأصله ، وناظرُ («الهداية» لا يخفى عليه أنّ التوجيه الذي ذكر هذا الناظر بعبارة المتن وافتخر به وطعن على الشارح الله له الذي هو أعلم منه بمقصودِ جده وأستاذه مؤلّف «الوقاية» بعيد بمراحل عن كلام صاحب «الهداية». ولعل العصام لم يتيسر له مطالعة عبارة «الهداية» وإلا لم يؤول بما أوّل عبارة «الوقاية».
ثم أقول : كلام المصنّف هاهنا لا يخلو عن تلخيص مخل، وذلك لأن صاحب «الهداية» ذكر أوّلاً في «باب ثبوتِ النسب» مسألةُ ولادة المعلق طلاقها بتزوجها، ثمّ مسألة نسب ولد المطلقة الرجعية ، ثم مسألة نسب ولد المبتوتة، ثمّ مسألة المطلقة الصغيرة، ثمّ مسألة نسب ولد المتوفى عنها زوجها ، ثمّ مسألة المعتدة المعترفة بانقضاء عدتها ، ثم شرع في بيان شرائط ثبوتِ النسب في المعتدة بقوله : إذا ولدت المعتدة ولداً لم يثبت نسبه عند أبي حنيفة إلا أن يشهد إلى آخر ما نقلناه سابقاً.
ثم قال : فإن كانت معتدة عن الوفاة فصدقها الورثة في الولادة ولم يشهد على الولادة أحد إلى آخر ما مر نقله سابقاً، فكلامه السابق لبيان مدة ثبوت النسب في معتدة وكلامه اللاحق لبيان شرائط ثبوته وكيفيته في معتدّة . ويظهر من كلامه أنّ ثبوت نسب ولدِ المعتدة عن طلاق رجعي أو بائن يكون بثبوت ولادتها بإحدى الطرق الثلاثة : قيام الشهادة، أو ظهور الحبل، أو اعتراف الزوج به عنده.
وعندهما بشهادة امرأةٍ واحدة، وثبوت نسب ولد المعتدة يكون بالطرق المذكورة، وبإقرار الورثة أيضاً.

The married woman who gives birth at six months, meaning she is not divorced but her marriage is ongoing, then if he denies her giving birth to this child, its establishment is confirmed by the testimony of one woman without stipulating these attributes. End. I say: Most commentators in this context have remained silent about the solution and refinement, and have not brought what clarifies. Al-'Isam, although he brought what many glosses lacked, yet he was not protected from slipping, for his speech is flawed in my view in several ways: First: What he chose involves clear affectation that the context and sequence reject. Second: The meaning of the word 'mu'taddah' which he made the subject must either mean only the mu'taddah of divorce or general including the mu'taddah of death. If the first is intended, then aside from this specification being without a specifier, his statement 'or she gives birth in less than two years and the heirs acknowledge it' is invalid, because this period is considered only for the woman whose husband died, not for the divorced woman; for in the revocable mu'taddah, lineage is established even if she gives birth after more than two years as long as she does not admit to the expiration of the iddah, and in the irrevocably divorced woman it is established even if she gives birth at the completion of two years, as detailed previously. I say: This, besides being not immediately understood, is invalidated by what invalidates the second possibility, namely he says later 'if he denies her giving birth', the pronoun of denial refers to the husband, as indicated by his statement after it 'so about if he denies him [؟]', and by the evidence of his earlier statement 'the husband acknowledged it or remained silent.' Third: It is apparent that his later statement contextually and sequentially, as we explained earlier, testifies that his saying 'if he denies' is an explanation of the husband's denial, and this cannot be imagined in the case of his death, so the predicate does not relate to the subject. Fourth: His statement 'if he denies her giving birth' is explicit that the purpose is denial of the birth itself, not denial of identification, so interpreting it otherwise is forced to the extreme. The truth is that his saying 'if he denies' is attached to his saying 'married woman' only, as you will soon see, God willing. Perhaps al-'Isam did not have the opportunity to study the wording of 'Al-Hidayah', otherwise he would not have interpreted the wording of 'Al-Wiqaya' as he did. Then I say: The author's speech here is not free from deficient summarization, because the author of 'Al-Hidayah' first mentioned in the 'Chapter on Establishment of Lineage' the issue of the birth of the one whose divorce was suspended upon her marriage, then the issue of the lineage of the child of the revocably divorced woman, then the issue of the lineage of the child of the irrevocably divorced woman, then the issue of the minor divorced woman, then the issue of the lineage of the child of the woman whose husband died, then the issue of the mu'taddah who admits the expiration of her iddah, then he began explaining the conditions for establishing lineage in the mu'taddah with his statement: 'When the mu'taddah gives birth to a child, his lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifa unless they testify...' up to what we previously transmitted. Then he said: 'If she is a mu'taddah from death, and the heirs believe her regarding the birth and no one testifies to the birth...' up to what was previously transmitted. So his earlier speech is to explain the period for establishing lineage in the mu'taddah, and his later speech is to explain the conditions for its establishment and its modality in the mu'taddah. It appears from his speech that the establishment of the lineage of the child of the mu'taddah from revocable or irrevocable divorce is by establishing her giving birth through one of three methods: establishment of testimony, or appearance of pregnancy, or the husband's acknowledgment of him according to him (Abu Hanifa). And according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) by the testimony of one woman. And the establishment of the lineage of the child of the mu'taddah (from death) is by the mentioned methods and also by the acknowledgment of the heirs. The author (of Al-Wiqaya) did well in summarizing the five issues that were in explaining the period considered in this chapter, but he did not mention the issue of the period of the mu'taddah whose husband died, and he discussed the topic of conditions for establishing...
Source pages p. 509

Commentary
This passage is a critical commentary (hashiya) on the interpretation of 'Al-Wiqaya' by a scholar named al-'Isam. The author of 'Umdat al-Ri'aya' raises five objections to al-'Isam's reading of a passage about paternity establishment for a woman in iddah. The core issue is the correct referent of 'mu'taddah' in the text: does it include both divorce and death iddah, or only divorce? Al-'Isam's attempt to use the rhetorical device 'istikhdam' (where one word is used in two senses) is rejected because it is not immediately clear and is contradicted by the context, which clearly refers to a husband's denial of birth—impossible in death. The author insists that the phrase 'if he denies' attaches to 'married woman' only, not to 'mu'taddah'. He also argues that al-'Isam's interpretation contradicts the source text of al-Hidayah. The passage then summarizes the correct Hanafi position from al-Hidayah: For a mu'taddah from divorce (revocable or irrevocable), paternity is established by one of three methods: testimony (two witnesses according to Abu Hanifa, one woman according to the two disciples), appearance of pregnancy, or the husband's acknowledgment. For a mu'taddah from death, an additional method is the acknowledgment of the heirs. The author commends the summary of the period issues but notes a deficiency in not covering the period for a death iddah.

Key Terms
المعتدة (al-mu'taddah): The woman observing iddah after divorce or death of husband.
الاستخدام (al-istikhdam): Rhetorical device where one word is used in two different senses in the same context.
المبتوتة (al-mabtutah): Irrevocably divorced woman.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The word 'mu'taddah' is ambiguous and cannot be specified.
B) The pronoun 'he' in 'if he denies' cannot refer to a deceased husband.
C) The rhetorical device istikhdam is not recognized in Hanafi usul.
D) The phrase about two years applies only to divorce iddah.

Key Takeaway
The term 'mu'taddah' in paternity establishment must be interpreted contextually; the husband's denial indicates divorce iddah, not death iddah, and heirs' acknowledgment is only relevant for death iddah.

Establishing Lineage of Child Born to Woman in 'Iddah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Witnesses and Conditions
Critical refinement on conditions for establishing lineage in 'iddah cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute on the number of witnesses required to establish the birth of a child from a woman in 'iddah, and distinguish between the evidentiary methods for birth vs. the conditions of time for lineage.

Core Idea
Lineage from a woman in 'iddah requires both valid proof of birth and birth within the correct period; heirs' acknowledgment only proves birth, not lineage.

This lesson examines the fine print of establishing lineage (thubut al-nasab) for a child born to a woman observing 'iddah. The passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah corrects a commentator who misunderstood the abridgment of al-Wiqayah from al-Hidayah. The central legal points involve the number of witnesses required to prove birth (with a dispute between Abu Hanifah and his two disciples) and the critical distinction that proving birth is only half the equation—the birth must also occur within the prescribed 'iddah period. Understanding these conditions ensures that lineage is only established when both requirements are satisfied.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central legal issue
The passage deals with the conditions for establishing the lineage of a child born to a woman in 'iddah. The primary question is: what evidence is needed to prove the birth, and does that evidence alone establish lineage?
The intra-Hanafi dispute focuses on the number of witnesses required to prove the birth.
2
Outline Abu Hanifah's position
According to Imam Abu Hanifah, the birth must be proven by the testimony of two men or one man and two women. This is the standard requirement for testimony in most matters.
Abu Hanifah treats birth testimony like any ordinary testimony.
3
Outline the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the testimony of a single woman suffices to prove the birth for purposes of lineage. They consider matters related to women's affairs as subject to a lower evidentiary threshold.
The Sahibayn's view is based on the nature of birth as a woman's matter.
4
Understand the four methods to prove birth
The passage identifies four ways to establish that a birth occurred: testimony (with the dispute above), appearance of pregnancy, the husband's acknowledgment, and (for widows) the heirs' acknowledgment. Each method proves only the birth event itself.
The method of proving birth must be valid; then the second condition must be checked.
5
Recognize the role of the 'iddah period
Even if birth is proven, lineage is not automatically established. The birth must have occurred within the correct 'iddah period for that type of divorce or widowhood. If the birth falls outside that period, no method can establish lineage.
The period varies: revocable divorce, irrevocable divorce, and death have different maximum durations.
6
Understand the correction about heirs' acknowledgment
The passage stresses that the heirs' acknowledgment (for widows) only takes the place of testimony in proving the birth itself—not in proving lineage. Therefore, if the birth occurs outside the widow's 'iddah period, the heirs' acknowledgment does not help.
Inserting the conjunction 'wa' in 'wa aqarra al-warathatu biha' clarifies that it refers to the birth, not lineage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ورابعها : إن قوله : فإن جحد ولادتها صريح في أنَّ الغرض منه إنكار نفس الولادة لا إنكار التعيين، فحمله عليه تعسّف أي تعسف والحق أن قوله : فإن جحد متعلق بقوله : منكوحة لا غير، كما ستطلع عليه عن قريب إن شاء الله.
وخامسها : إنّ «الوقاية» لما كانت ملخّصة ومأخوذة من «الهداية» لا بد أن يجعل تلخيصه موافقاً لأصله ، وناظرُ («الهداية» لا يخفى عليه أنّ التوجيه الذي ذكر هذا الناظر بعبارة المتن وافتخر به وطعن على الشارح [؟] الله له الذي هو أعلم منه بمقصودِ جده وأستاذه مؤلّف «الوقاية» بعيد بمراحل عن كلام صاحب «الهداية». ولعل العصام لم يتيسر له مطالعة عبارة «الهداية» وإلا لم يؤول بما أوّل عبارة «الوقاية».
ثم أقول : كلام المصنّف هاهنا لا يخلو عن تلخيص مخل، وذلك لأن صاحب «الهداية» ذكر أوّلاً في «باب ثبوتِ النسب» مسألةُ ولادة المعلق طلاقها بتزوجها، ثمّ مسألة نسب ولد المطلقة الرجعية ، ثم مسألة نسب ولد المبتوتة، ثمّ مسألة المطلقة الصغيرة، ثمّ مسألة نسب ولد المتوفى عنها زوجها ، ثمّ مسألة المعتدة المعترفة بانقضاء عدتها ، ثم شرع في بيان شرائط ثبوتِ النسب في المعتدة بقوله : إذا ولدت المعتدة ولداً لم يثبت نسبه عند أبي حنيفة إلا أن يشهد إلى آخر ما نقلناه سابقاً.
ثم قال : فإن كانت معتدة عن الوفاة فصدقها الورثة في الولادة ولم يشهد على الولادة أحد إلى آخر ما مر نقله سابقاً، فكلامه السابق لبيان مدة ثبوت النسب في معتدة وكلامه اللاحق لبيان شرائط ثبوته وكيفيته في معتدّة . ويظهر من كلامه أنّ ثبوت نسب ولدِ المعتدة عن طلاق رجعي أو بائن يكون بثبوت ولادتها بإحدى الطرق الثلاثة : قيام الشهادة، أو ظهور الحبل، أو اعتراف الزوج به عنده.
وعندهما بشهادة امرأةٍ واحدة، وثبوت نسب ولد المعتدة يكون بالطرق المذكورة، وبإقرار الورثة أيضاً.
والمصنف له أحسن في تلخيص المسائل الخمسة التي كانت في بيان المدة المعتبرة في هذا الباب، ولم يذكر مسألة مدة المعتدة المتوفى عنها زوجها، وذكر بحث شرائط ثبوت النسب بقوله : ومعتدة ظهر حبلها ... الخ، على وجه يتضمّن ذكر مدة المعتدة عن وفاة ، حيث قال : أو ولدت لأقل من سنتين....الخ.
فجاء الخلل في تلخيصه من حيث أنه خلط مسائل مدة ثبوتِ النَّسب مع مسائل شرائط ثبوت النسب، ونظمها في سلك واحد ، فيتوهم منه أنّ المعتدة المذكورة بقوله : ومعتدة ظهر حبلها ... الخ، المعطوفة على معتدّة الرجعي غير المعتدّات المذكورة مع أنها تشملها وغيرها، وهو معتدة الوفاة.
وبعد ذلك أقول : كلام الشارح [؟] هاهنا لا يخلو عن سوء الفهم، وذلك لأنّ ناظر کلام «الهداية» من أوله إلى آخره يعلم قطعاً أن مقصوده : أن ثبوت الولادة الذي هو مدار ثبوت النسب يكون بإحدى الطرق الأربعة : ظهور الحبل، واعتراف الزوج به، وقيام الشهادة، وإقرار الورثة بها، وهذا خاص بمعتدة الوفاة.
وإن هذه الأمور إنما تعتبر إذا اعتبرت المدة المعينة لكل معتدة، مثلاً إن قامت الشهادة على أنّ المبتوتة ولدت ولداً لا تعتبر ذلك ما لم يعلم كونها في المدة التي يثبتُ نسب ولد المبتوتة فيها، وكذا إن أقرّ الورثة بولادة المتوفى عنها زوجها لا يكفي ذلك في ثبوت النسب، بل إذا كانت المدة تحتمله.
وبالجملة : لا بد في ثبوت نسب ولد المعتدات من كون الولادة في المدة المقرة لكل منها، مع ثبوتِ الولادة بإحدى الطرق المذكورة. والحاصل : إن إقرار الورثة إنما قامَ مقامَ الشهادة في إثباتِ نفس الولادة، لا في ثبوتِ النسب مطلقاً، فكما أنَّ الشهادة على نفس الولادة لا تفيد إذا كانت خارج المدة كذلك إقرار الورثة لا يعتبر إلا إذا كانت المدّة قابلة لثبوت النسب، وإن المراد بإقرار الورثة إقرارهم بنفس ولادتها مع قطع النظرِ عن الإقرار بثبوتِ نسب الولد من الزوج. إذا عرفت هذا كله فأعرف : إنّ الصواب هو إيراد كلمة الواو في قوله : وأقر الورثة بها ؛ أي بالولادة، والشارح لما لم يفهم كنه المقصود ، ولم يتيسر له تطابق المتن بـ«الهداية» حكم بما حكم.
(۱) العلماء المحققون الذين تتبعوا «الوقاية وشرحها ، مثل: ((الدرر» (١ : ٤٠٨)، و«الإيضاح» (ق ۹۲/أ)، و(مجمع الأنهر » (۱) : (٤٧٧) لم يوافقوا الشارح له فيما ذهب إليه، بل مشوا على عبارة «الوقاية».
Fourth: His statement 'if he denies her giving birth' is explicit that the intent is denial of the birth itself, not denial of specification; interpreting it otherwise is far-fetched. The truth is that his statement 'if he denies' is connected to his statement 'married woman', nothing else, as you will see shortly, God willing. Fifth: Since al-Wiqayah is an abridgment taken from al-Hidayah, its abridgment must correspond to its original. A viewer of al-Hidayah does not overlook that the interpretation that this commentator mentioned in the text, boasting about it and criticizing the commentator (may God forgive him) who knows better than him the intent of his grandfather and teacher, the author of al-Wiqayah, is far removed from the words of the author of al-Hidayah. Perhaps al-Isam was not able to examine the wording of al-Hidayah; otherwise he would not have interpreted the wording of al-Wiqayah as he did. Then I say: The author's words here are not free from flawed abridgment. This is because the author of al-Hidayah first mentioned in the Chapter of Establishing Lineage the case of the birth of one whose divorce was suspended upon her marriage, then the case of the lineage of the child of a revocably divorced woman, then the case of the lineage of the child of an irrevocably divorced woman, then the case of the divorced minor, then the case of the lineage of the child of a woman whose husband died, then the case of the woman in 'iddah who acknowledges the end of her 'iddah. Then he began to explain the conditions for establishing lineage for a woman in 'iddah, saying: 'When a woman in 'iddah gives birth to a child, his lineage is not established according to Abu Hanifah unless witnesses testify...' up to what we previously transmitted. Then he said: 'If she is in 'iddah due to death, and the heirs believe her regarding the birth, and no one testified to the birth...' up to what was previously transmitted. So his earlier words explain the period for establishing lineage for a woman in 'iddah, and his later words explain the conditions for its establishment and its modality for a woman in 'iddah. It appears from his words that the establishment of the lineage of the child of a woman in 'iddah due to revocable or irrevocable divorce occurs by establishing her birth through one of three methods: testimony, appearance of pregnancy, or the husband's acknowledgment according to him (Abu Hanifah). According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), (it occurs) by the testimony of a single woman. The establishment of the lineage of the child of a woman in 'iddah occurs by the mentioned methods and also by the acknowledgment of the heirs. The author (of al-Wiqayah) did well in summarizing the five issues that deal with the period considered in this chapter, but he did not mention the issue of the period for a woman in 'iddah due to her husband's death. He mentioned the discussion of the conditions for establishing lineage by saying: 'A woman in 'iddah whose pregnancy appears...' etc., in a manner that includes mentioning the period for a woman in 'iddah due to death, where he said: 'or she gave birth in less than two years...etc.' Thus the defect in his abridgment is that he mixed the issues of the period for establishing lineage with the issues of the conditions for establishing lineage, and arranged them in a single thread. So it may be understood that the woman in 'iddah mentioned by his statement 'A woman in 'iddah whose pregnancy appears...' etc., conjoined with the woman in revocable 'iddah, is not among the women in 'iddah mentioned, while it covers her and others, namely the woman in 'iddah due to death. After that I say: The commentator's words here are not free from misunderstanding. This is because a viewer of the words of al-Hidayah from beginning to end knows with certainty that its intent is that establishing the birth, which is the basis for establishing lineage, occurs through one of four methods: appearance of pregnancy, the husband's acknowledgment, testimony, and the heirs' acknowledgment of it. And this is specific to the woman in 'iddah due to death. These matters are only considered when the specific period for each woman in 'iddah is considered. For example, if testimony is established that the irrevocably divorced woman gave birth to a child, it is not considered unless it is known that it was within the period in which the lineage of the child of an irrevocably divorced woman is established. Similarly, if the heirs acknowledge the birth of a woman whose husband died, that is not sufficient for establishing lineage unless the period allows it. In summary, to establish the lineage of the child of women in 'iddah, the birth must occur within the period prescribed for each of them, along with establishing the birth through one of the mentioned methods. The conclusion is that the heirs' acknowledgment only takes the place of testimony in establishing the birth itself, not in establishing lineage absolutely. Just as testimony to the birth itself is not useful if it falls outside the period, similarly the heirs' acknowledgment is not considered unless the period is capable of establishing lineage. What is meant by the heirs' acknowledgment is their acknowledgment of the birth itself, disregarding acknowledgment of the establishment of the child's lineage from the husband. Since you have recognized all this, know that the correct thing is to insert the conjunction 'wa' in his statement 'wa aqarra al-warathatu biha', i.e., by the birth. The commentator, because he did not understand the essence of the intent and could not align the text with al-Hidayah, ruled as he ruled. (1) The verifying scholars who followed al-Wiqayah and its commentary, such as al-Durar (1:408), al-Idah (q 92/a), and Majma' al-Anhur (1:477), did not agree with the commentator regarding what he went to; rather they followed the wording of al-Wiqayah.
Source pages p. 510

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah, analyzing the abridgment of al-Wiqayah from al-Hidayah regarding the conditions for establishing the lineage of a child born to a woman in 'iddah. The author critiques a commentator who misunderstood the structure and intended meaning. The key legal issue involves the number of witnesses required: according to Imam Abu Hanifah, lineage is established only with the testimony of two men or one man and two women, whereas according to the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the testimony of one woman suffices. The author also identifies four methods to establish the birth itself: testimony, appearance of pregnancy, husband's acknowledgment, and (specifically for the widow) the heirs' acknowledgment. However, these methods only establish the birth; lineage also requires the birth to occur within the correct 'iddah period. The author corrects the commentator by insisting that the heirs' acknowledgment is only for the birth event, not for lineage, and that the conjunction 'wa' must be included in the phrase 'wa aqarra al-warathatu biha' to clarify that it refers to the birth. Scholars following al-Wiqayah agreed with the author's correction.

Key Terms
ثبوت النسب (thubut al-nasab): Establishment of legal lineage between a child and his father, with all attendant rights of inheritance, custody, and maintenance.
المعتدة (al-mu'taddah): A woman observing the waiting period ('iddah) after divorce or death of husband, during which she cannot remarry.
إقرار الورثة (iqrar al-warathah): Acknowledgment by the heirs of the deceased husband that the widow gave birth, which serves as proof of the birth event only, not lineage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the passage criticize the commentator's reading of al-Wiqayah?
A) He misinterpreted the number of witnesses required.
B) He mixed the issues of time period for lineage with the conditions for proving birth.
C) He omitted the case of the widow entirely.
D) He used a weak hadith as evidence.

Key Takeaway
For a child born to a woman in 'iddah, lineage requires both valid proof of birth (through one of four methods) and that birth occurs within the correct 'iddah period; the intra-Hanafi dispute on witness count does not affect this condition.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Establishing Paternity in Widow's Iddah: The Role of Heirs' Acknowledgment
Critique of a commentator's misinterpretation of paternity proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the correct Hanafi distinction between proof of birth and proof of paternity in a widow's iddah, and apply it to cases involving heirs' acknowledgment.

Core Idea
Heirs' acknowledgment proves birth, not paternity; paternity requires birth within the two-year period.

This lesson clarifies a common misunderstanding in Hanafi fiqh regarding the role of the heirs' acknowledgment in establishing the paternity of a child born to a widow. The passage comes from a hashiah correcting a commentator of al-Wiqayah who conflated the conditions for proof of birth with the conditions for proof of lineage. You will learn the four methods to prove birth and how the permissible period (maximum two years after the husband's death) is an independent requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four methods of proving birth
From the passage, list the four ways to establish that the widow gave birth: appearance of pregnancy, husband's acknowledgment, testimony, and heirs' acknowledgment.
These methods are specific to the widow; the passage emphasizes this.
2
Distinguish between proof of birth and proof of paternity
Understand that birth must be proven by one of the four methods, but paternity (attributing the child to the deceased husband) also requires that the birth occurred within the specific iddah period for a widow, which is a maximum of two years after death.
The commentator mixed these two independent elements.
3
Understand the role of heirs' acknowledgment
The heirs' acknowledgment only stands in place of testimony to prove the fact of birth itself. It does not assert that the child is from the deceased.
The correct Arabic in al-Wiqayah includes the conjunction 'بها' (referring to birth), not 'به' (the child).
4
Apply the two-year rule for widow's iddah
For a widow, paternity is established only if the birth occurs within two years from the husband's death. If the birth is outside this period, even if the heirs acknowledge, paternity is not established.
This is based on a hadith and is specific to Hanafi fiqh.
5
Recognize the commentator's error and the correct reading
The commentator misunderstood the text and thought heirs' acknowledgment directly proves paternity. The author of the hashiah corrects this by citing later authorities (al-Durar, al-Idah, Majma' al-Anhur) who upheld the original wording.
The error leads to a practical consequence: under the commentator's view, a child born after two years could be attributed to the deceased; under the correct view, it cannot.

كتاب الطلاق باب ثبوت النسب والحضانة

النسب بقوله : ومعتدة ظهر حبلها ... الخ، على وجه يتضمّن ذكر مدة المعتدة عن وفاة ، حيث قال : أو ولدت لأقل من سنتين....الخ.
فجاء الخلل في تلخيصه من حيث أنه خلط مسائل مدة ثبوتِ النَّسب مع مسائل شرائط ثبوت النسب، ونظمها في سلك واحد ، فيتوهم منه أنّ المعتدة المذكورة بقوله : ومعتدة ظهر حبلها ... الخ، المعطوفة على معتدّة الرجعي غير المعتدّات المذكورة مع أنها تشملها وغيرها، وهو معتدة الوفاة.
وبعد ذلك أقول : كلام الشارح لالا لاله هاهنا لا يخلو عن سوء الفهم، وذلك لأنّ ناظر كلام «الهداية» من أوله إلى آخره يعلم قطعاً أن مقصوده : أن ثبوت الولادة الذي هو مدار ثبوت النسب يكون بإحدى الطرق الأربعة : ظهور الحبل، واعتراف الزوج به، وقيام الشهادة، وإقرار الورثة بها، وهذا خاص بمعتدة الوفاة.
وإن هذه الأمور إنما تعتبر إذا اعتبرت المدة المعينة لكل معتدة، مثلاً إن قامت الشهادة على أنّ المبتوتة ولدت ولداً لا تعتبر ذلك ما لم يعلم كونها في المدة التي يثبتُ نسب ولد المبتوتة فيها، وكذا إن أقرّ الورثة بولادة المتوفى عنها زوجها لا يكفي ذلك في ثبوت النسب، بل إذا كانت المدة تحتمله.
وبالجملة : لا بد في ثبوت نسب ولد المعتدات من كون الولادة في المدة المقررة لكل منها، مع ثبوتِ الولادة بإحدى الطرق المذكورة. والحاصل : إن إقرار الورثة إنما قامَ  َمقامَ الشهادة في إثباتِ نفس الولادة، لا في ثبوتِ النسب مطلقاً، فكما أنَّ الشهادة على نفس الولادة لا تفيد إذا كانت خارج المدة كذلك إقرار الورثة لا يعتبر إلا إذا كانت المدّة قابلة لثبوت النسب، وإن المراد بإقرار الورثة إقرارهم بنفس ولادتها مع قطع النظرِ عن الإقرار بثبوتِ نسب الولد من الزوج. إذا عرفت هذا كله فأعرف : إنّ الصواب هو إيراد كلمة الواو في قوله : وأقر الورثة بها ؛ أي بالولادة، والشارح لما لم يفهم كنه المقصود ، ولم يتيسر له تطابق المتن بـ«الهداية» حكم بما حكم
وقد
العلماء المحققون الذين تتبعوا «الوقاية وشرحها ، مثل : ((الدرر» (١ : ٤٠٨)، و«الإيضاح» (ق ۹۲/أ)، و(مجمع الأنهر » (۱) : (٤٧٧) لم يوافقوا الشارح له فيما ذهب إليه، بل مشوا على
عبارة «الوقاية».

إلى هذا النمط: أو تثبت ولادتها بحجةٍ تامة، أو عُلِمَ أَنَّها وَلَدَتْ بعد وفاته لأقل من سنتين، أو لم يُعلَم وأقر الورثة به.
فقوله : أو لم يعلم... إلى آخره ، يشمل ما إذا لم يُعْلَمْ أَنَّه وُلِدَ قبل الموت ، أو بعده وعلى تقدير العلم بأنَّ ولادتَهُ بعد موتِ الزَّوج لا يعلمُ أَنَّه وُلِدَ لأقل من سنتين ، أو لسنتين ، أو أكثر، لكن أقر الورثة أنّ هذا الولد ولد مورثهم ، فإذا أقروا بذلك
فاحفظ هذا كله مع ما يأتي بعده ، وانظمه في سلك النفائس المنشورة في هذه الحواشي ، وتعجب من شراح المتن ومحشي الشرح كيف يغفلون عن حل مثل هذه المواضع ، ويكتفون على إيراد الأمر الواضح، مع الغفلة عن تنقيح الأمر الواقع، وبالله العجب من أكثر محشي الشرح لا يصلون إلى ما يفيد ويغني، ويكتفون بذكر ما لا يفيد ولا
يغني.
[١] قوله : إلى هذا النمط ؛ فيه أنّ هذا النمط غير موافق مقصوده بمقصود صاحب «الهداية كما ذكرناه مشرحاً ، فكيف يصح تغيير كلام «الوقاية» التي هي ملخصة «الهداية» إليه فضلا عن أن يجب ولعمري ؛ لو نظر الشارح له حين هذا التحرير في
«الهداية» لم يقع في هذا الحكم البعيد عن الدراية.
[٢]قوله : يشمل ... الخ ؛ يعني تدخل فيه صورتان :
أحدهما : إن لم يعلم أنّ ذلك الولد ولد قبل الموت أو بعده.
وآخرهما : أن لا يعلم أنَّ ولادته بعد موتِ الزوج لأقل من سنتين أو لتمامها أو
لأكثر منهما.
ففي هاتين الصورتين إذا أقرت الورثة كونَ ذلك الولد من مورثهم كفى ذلك
لثبوت النسب.
(۳) قوله : إن هذا الولد ... الخ ؛ أقول : هذا صريح في أن الشارح له فهم أن الإقرار المذكور هاهنا المراد به إقرار الورثة بأنّ هذا الولد ولد مورثهم، فبنى عليه ما بني، وهو غير صحيح، فإنّ ناظر كلام «الهداية» و«الوقاية» يحكم قطعاً بأنّ المراد به إقرار نفس الولادة، وأما النسب فيثبت بكونه في مدّة يثبت فيهما نسب ولد المعتدة المتوفى عنها زوجها، فافهم.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Establishing Lineage and Custody. Lineage by his statement: 'And a woman in waiting period whose pregnancy becomes apparent... etc.' in a manner that includes mentioning the period of the widow's waiting period, where he said: 'Or she gave birth in less than two years... etc.' So the defect in his summary came from the fact that he mixed the issues of the period of establishing lineage with the issues of the conditions of establishing lineage, and organized them in one thread. So it is misunderstood from him that the mentioned waiting woman by his statement: 'And a woman in waiting period whose pregnancy becomes apparent... etc.' is conjoined to the waiting woman of revocable divorce, not including the other waiting women mentioned, while it includes them and others, and it is the widow. After that I say: The commentator's speech here is not free from misunderstanding, because the one who considers the speech of al-Hidayah from its beginning to its end knows definitely that its purpose is that the establishment of birth, which is the basis of establishing lineage, is by one of four methods: appearance of pregnancy, the husband's acknowledgment of it, establishing testimony, and the acknowledgment of the heirs to it. And this is specific to the widow. And these matters are only considered if the specific period for each waiting woman is considered. For example, if testimony is established that a permanently divorced woman gave birth to a child, that is not considered unless it is known that she was in the period in which the lineage of the child of the permanently divorced woman is established. Similarly, if the heirs acknowledge the birth of the woman whose husband died, that is not sufficient for establishing lineage, but only if the period is capable of it. In summary: For establishing the lineage of the child of women in waiting periods, it is necessary that the birth occurs in the period prescribed for each, along with the establishment of birth by one of the mentioned methods. The result: The acknowledgment of the heirs only takes the place of testimony in proving the birth itself, not in establishing lineage absolutely. So just as testimony about the birth itself is not useful if it is outside the period, similarly the acknowledgment of the heirs is only considered if the period is capable of establishing lineage. And what is meant by the acknowledgment of the heirs is their acknowledgment of the birth itself, regardless of the acknowledgment of establishing the lineage of the child from the husband. When you know all this, then know that the correct thing is to insert the letter waw in his statement: 'and the heirs acknowledge it'; i.e., the birth. And because the commentator did not understand the essence of the purpose, and it was not possible for him to match the text with al-Hidayah, he judged what he judged. And the investigating scholars who followed al-Wiqayah and its commentary, such as al-Durar (1:408), al-Idah (folio 92/a), and Majma' al-Anhur (1:477), did not agree with the commentator in what he went to, but rather followed the wording of al-Wiqayah. [He said] 'in this manner: or her birth is established by a complete proof, or it is known that she gave birth after his death in less than two years, or it is not known and the heirs acknowledge it.' So his statement: 'or it is not known... etc.' includes two cases: one: that it is not known whether that child was born before death or after it. The second: that it is not known that his birth after the husband's death was for less than two years, or for two years, or more. In these two cases, if the heirs acknowledge that that child is from their testator, that is sufficient for establishing lineage. [The commentator's statement] 'that this child... etc.' I say: This is explicit that the commentator understood that the acknowledgment mentioned here is meant as the acknowledgment of the heirs that this child is the child of their testator, and he built upon that what he built, and it is incorrect. Because the one who considers the speech of al-Hidayah and al-Wiqayah judges definitely that what is meant by it is the acknowledgment of the birth itself. As for lineage, it is established by it being in a period in which the lineage of the child of the widow is established, so understand.
Source pages p. 511

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from a hashiah (super-commentary) on the commentary of al-Wiqayah. The author is correcting a serious misunderstanding made by the original commentator (شارح) regarding the rules for establishing paternity (نسب) in the case of a widow's waiting period (عدة الوفاة). The commentator had confused the conditions for the duration of the waiting period with the conditions for proving paternity. The author clarifies that the establishment of paternity depends on two independent elements: first, proof of the birth itself, which can be established by four methods: visible pregnancy, the husband's acknowledgment, testimony, or acknowledgment by the heirs; second, that the birth occurs within the specific timeframe for that type of iddah. For a widow, the maximum period for paternity is two years after the husband's death. The acknowledgment of the heirs only serves to prove the fact of birth, not the paternity directly. Therefore, even if heirs acknowledge, if the birth occurred outside the permissible period, paternity is not established. The correct reading of the text in al-Wiqayah is with a conjunction (واو) in the phrase 'وأقر الورثة بها' meaning 'and the heirs acknowledge it (the birth)'. The author cites later authorities (al-Durar, al-Idah, Majma' al-Anhur) who upheld the original wording of al-Wiqayah and rejected the commentator's interpretation.

Key Terms
إقرار الورثة (iqrar al-warathah): The acknowledgment by the heirs of the deceased husband that the widow gave birth; it serves as proof of the birth itself, not directly of paternity.
معتدة الوفاة (mu'taddat al-wafat): A widow who is in her waiting period after her husband's death. Her iddah is four months and ten days unless she is pregnant, in which case it extends until delivery.
ثبوت النسب (thubut al-nasab): The legal establishment of lineage or paternity of a child to his father. In this context, it requires both valid proof of birth and the birth occurring within the recognized timeframe of the iddah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct Hanafi position explained in the passage, what is the function of the heirs' acknowledgment (إقرار الورثة) in a widow's iddah?
A) It directly establishes the child's paternity to the deceased husband.
B) It proves the fact of the widow's birth, and paternity is established only if the birth occurred within the permissible period.
C) It replaces the need for any time period requirement.
D) It is only valid if the widow herself acknowledges the paternity.

Key Takeaway
In widow's iddah, heirs' acknowledgment only proves the birth; paternity requires the birth to be within the two-year period.

Minimum Pregnancy Duration and Woman's Claim without Oath
Intra-Hanafi dispute on paternity and woman's credibility without oath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi intra-school dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding a woman's claim of marriage timing for paternity, and identify the practical consequence of each view.

Core Idea
In paternity disputes, Abu Hanifa trusts the apparent circumstance of lawful marriage; the Sahibayn require an oath.

This passage from the Kitab al-Talaq deals with a nuanced scenario: a woman gives birth and claims the marriage was six months ago, making the child legitimate. The husband denies this, claiming the marriage was less than six months. Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, disagree on how to resolve this — specifically whether the woman must take an oath to establish her claim. Understanding this ikhtilaf reveals how the Hanafi school balances textual proof (al-zahir) against procedural justice.

Guided Path
1
State the base ruling
Paternity is not established if the child is born less than six months after marriage. This is agreed upon by all.
The six-month period is derived from minimum pregnancy duration.
2
Identify the scenario of dispute
The woman claims the marriage was six months ago; the husband claims it was less. The child's paternity hinges on whose word is accepted.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa says the woman is believed without oath because the apparent circumstance (al-zahir) is that Muslims engage in lawful intercourse, so the child is presumed from marriage.
He also holds that in matters of lineage and marriage, the denier is not put to oath.
4
State the Sahibayn's position and proof
The two companions require the woman to take an oath (or refuse) if the husband has no evidence, because the husband's denial creates doubt, and establishing lineage against his claim requires evidence.
5
Note the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, paternity is established immediately. Under Sahibayn, paternity is established only if the woman takes the oath or the husband's denial fails.
This difference shows a tension between substantive justice (protecting lineage) and procedural fairness (heeding the husband's denial).

وعنده يصدق قولها، ولا تحلفُ بناءً على أنّ النسب والنكاح من الأشياء التي لا يحلف فيها المنكر عنده، على ما سيأتي تفصيله إن شاء الله في «كتاب الدعوى»، وقد ذكرنا نبذاً منه سابقاً فتذكره.
[٣] قوله : لا من السفاح ؛ - بكسر السين - بمعنى الزنا، والحاصل : إن الظاهر يشهد لها ، فإنّها تدعي ما يكون به الولد ثابتُ النَّسب من الزوج، والعلوق بالوطء الحلال لا من الحرام، والظاهرُ من حال كل مسلم ومسلمة هو هذا.
For less than it (six months) paternity is not established. If she gives birth and claims her marriage was six months ago, while the husband claims less, she is believed without an oath according to Abu Hanifa. Because the apparent circumstance witnesses for her that the child is from marriage, not from fornication. If you say: Li'an here becomes obligatory by denying the child, and its existence has been established by the testimony of one woman, so it would necessitate establishing li'an by the testimony of one woman, whereas they have stated that li'an is in the meaning of hudud, which are not established by women's testimony. I say: The obligation of li'an is only by qadhf (accusation of adultery), and that exists here by his saying 'this is not from me', and qadhf does not entail the existence of the child, for it is valid without it. This is in al-Nihaya and al-Inaya. [1] His saying: 'and for less than it' means when a married woman gives birth less than six months from the time of marriage, his paternity is not established from the husband, because such conception from him is not conceivable. [2] His saying: 'if she gives birth...etc.' means if a married woman gives birth and she differs with the husband, the husband says 'I married you and not even six months have passed, rather less', and she says 'you married me six months ago', her goal is to compel the husband to accept the child's lineage, and his goal is to deny it because the child is born less than six months from the time of the marriage. According to them (the two companions), she is made to take an oath if the husband does not produce evidence, and it is decided by her oath or refusal. According to him (Abu Hanifa), her statement is believed and she is not made to take an oath, based on the fact that lineage and marriage are among things in which the denier is not made to take an oath according to him, as will be detailed in the Book of Claims, and we have mentioned something of it earlier, so remember it. [3] His saying: 'not from fornication' - with kasr of the sin - meaning zina, and the conclusion is that the apparent circumstance witnesses for her, for she claims that by which the child's lineage from the husband is established, and conception is by lawful intercourse not unlawful, and the apparent circumstance of every Muslim man and woman is this.
Source pages p. 515

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the establishment of paternity and the credibility of a woman's claim about the timing of her marriage. The base ruling is that if a woman gives birth less than six months after marriage, paternity is not established (this is agreed upon). The dispute arises when the woman claims the marriage was six months ago (making the child's paternity valid) and the husband claims it was less. According to Abu Hanifa, the woman is believed without oath because the apparent circumstance (al-zahir) supports her: Muslims are presumed to engage in lawful intercourse, not fornication. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) require her to take an oath because the husband denies and the claim involves establishing a legal right (lineage) against him. The text anticipates an objection: if one woman's testimony establishes the child's existence, then li'an (mutual cursing) could be established by a woman's testimony, but li'an is like hudud which require male witnesses. The response is that li'an is not based on the child's existence but on the husband's qadhf (his statement 'this is not my child'), which does not require the child's existence. The commentary then explains each part: the condition for paternity (six months), the dispute with the two companions, and the basis for Abu Hanifa's position (the apparent circumstance of lawful intercourse).

Key Terms
الظاهر (al-zahir): The apparent circumstance or external evidence that supports a claim; used as legal proof.
السفاح (al-sifah): Fornication (zina), unlawful sexual intercourse.
اللعان (al-li'an): Mutual cursing between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery and she denies; it results in separation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, paternity disputes are influenced by the principle of al-zahir, leading to an intra-school split on whether the woman must take an oath.

Suspended Divorce and the Midwife's Testimony: Scope of Necessity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on proof of birth for suspended divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the effect of a midwife's testimony for a suspended divorce, and apply the principle 'al-thabit bi al-darurah yuqaddar bi qadriha' to distinguish between direct and consequential legal effects.

Core Idea
A testimony accepted by necessity cannot extend beyond its immediate purpose to trigger a separate legal consequence.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a husband who suspends his wife's divorce on her giving birth. The wife gives birth, but the husband denies it. Only a midwife testifies. Does the divorce occur? The answer depends on whether the testimony's scope is limited to establishing birth or extends to its legal consequences. We will analyze the arguments of Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the facts and the dispute
The husband says 'If I marry you and you give birth, you are divorced.' He marries her, she gives birth, the husband denies it, and a midwife testifies. Abu Hanifa says divorce does not occur; the Sahibayn say it does.
The condition of divorce is birth; the debate is about what evidence proves it.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's argument
They argue: birth is established by the midwife's testimony (accepted by necessity), and since divorce is suspended on birth, it follows as a necessary consequence. Many things are proven indirectly by what they depend on.
They see divorce as a legal consequence (taba'iyya) of the proven birth.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's argument
He argues: the testimony is accepted only out of necessity (darurah) to prove birth, and what is established by necessity is limited to its scope. Divorce is not a necessary consequence of birth because each can exist without the other. Therefore, the testimony does not extend to prove divorce.
The key principle: 'al-thabit bi al-darurah yuqaddar bi qadriha' (what is established by necessity is restricted to its extent).
4
Identify the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the wife remains married (no divorce). Under the Sahibayn, she becomes divorced upon the midwife's testimony. The text does not give a definitive tarjih; both views are transmitted.
This dispute has direct consequences for the marital status of the woman.
5
Apply the principle to new cases
Consider whether a midwife's testimony can be used to prove other consequences of birth, such as inheritance rights or iddah. Abu Hanifa's principle would limit it strictly to lineage-related matters, while the Sahibayn might extend it to consequences that are inseparable from birth.
This shows the importance of defining the scope of necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he suspended her divorce on her giving birth, and one woman testified to it, it does not occur – this according to Abu Hanifa, and according to them (the two companions) it does occur, because birth is established by the testimony of one woman, and then divorce is established by way of consequence. And for him: birth is established by the testimony of one woman out of necessity, so it is estimated by its own extent, so it does not extend to divorce, and it (divorce) is not a consequence of it, because each can exist without the other. [1] His saying: 'And if he suspended...etc.' means if he said to a woman: 'If I marry you and you give birth, then you are divorced', and he married her and she gave birth after, and the husband denied the birth, and a midwife testified to it, divorce does not occur by this testimony, even though lineage would be established if the birth was at six months or more; and according to them (the two companions), divorce occurs. (2) His saying: 'Because birth...' the summary: birth is established by the testimony of the midwife, and divorce, although not established by the testimony of a single woman, is here suspended on birth, so it is like its necessary consequence, so it is established by its establishment. And many things are not established by something directly but are established by way of consequence. (3) His saying: 'And for him' meaning for Abu Hanifa, and its summary: the establishment of birth by the testimony of one woman is only out of necessity, and that is that this situation is one where men are not present, and most often the midwife is present at birth, so if her statement were not considered, great hardship would result. Therefore al-Zuhri said: 'The Sunnah has passed that the testimony of women is permissible in matters that no one else sees,' transmitted by Ibn Abi Shayba, and what is established by necessity is estimated by its own extent, so it does not extend to other matters, so divorce is not established by such testimony. (4) His saying: 'And it is not...' is a response to what they said that divorce is established in this case as a consequence of birth, and its summary: divorce is not a consequence of birth, because each can exist without the other: divorce can occur without birth, and birth can occur without it if not suspended on it, and something with this nature is not a consequence.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the effect of a single woman's testimony on a suspended divorce. The case: a husband says to a woman, 'If I marry you and you give birth, you are divorced.' He marries her and she gives birth, but the husband denies the birth. A midwife testifies to the birth. According to Abu Hanifa, the divorce does not occur based on this testimony. According to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), the divorce does occur. Their reasoning: birth is established by the testimony of a single woman (midwife) by necessity, and since the divorce is suspended on birth, it follows as a necessary consequence. Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the birth is established only out of necessity (to avoid hardship), and what is established by necessity is limited to its scope. The necessity exists only for establishing the birth itself (for lineage and related matters), but it does not extend to establish divorce. Furthermore, divorce is not a necessary consequence of birth; each can exist independently (a woman can give birth without being divorced, and a man can divorce without birth). The commentary explains that this ruling applies provided the husband does not acknowledge the pregnancy and the pregnancy is not apparent. The text also cites al-Zuhri's statement about the permissibility of women's testimony in matters not witnessed by men.

Key Terms
تعليق الطلاق (ta'liq al-talaq): Suspending the occurrence of divorce upon a future condition; here, the condition is birth.
القابلة (al-qabila): Midwife; a woman who assists in childbirth; her testimony is accepted by necessity in matters of birth.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity; a legal concept that allows relaxation of normal rules to avoid hardship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because the husband did not witness the birth himself
C) Because the midwife's testimony is accepted only for the birth itself out of necessity, and divorce is not a necessary consequence
D) Because divorce requires two male witnesses

Key Takeaway
A testimony accepted out of necessity cannot be extended to prove a separate legal effect that is not a necessary consequence of the proven fact.

Suspended Divorce and the Testimony of a Single Woman
Intra-Hanafi dispute on testimony of a single woman proving childbirth for suspended divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the effect of a single woman's testimony in a suspended divorce and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa vs the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
What is established by necessity stays within its limits — testimony for birth does not extend to divorce.

A husband suspends divorce on his wife's childbirth; only a midwife testifies to the birth. Does the divorce occur? The Hanafi school splits: Abu Hanifa says no, the two companions say yes. The disagreement turns on the scope of necessity-based evidence and the nature of dependency between the condition and its consequence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
State the ruling according to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Note that the matn presents Abu Hanifa's view first.
The dispute is over the legal effect of a single woman's testimony.
2
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Understand why they argue the divorce occurs: childbirth is proven by the midwife, and the divorce is suspended on it, so it follows as a necessary consequence.
They invoke the principle that many things are established secondarily.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa responds: the testimony is accepted by necessity only for private matters; therefore it is limited to its immediate purpose (lineage). The divorce is not a true dependency because each can exist without the other.
The key maxim: al-ḍarūra tuqaddar bi-qadrihā.
4
Examine the hadith evidence
The hadith of al-Zuhri (mursal) limits women's testimony to matters only they can see. This supports confinement.
The hadith is zanni al-thubut but considered strong enough.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: in a dispute with only a midwife testifying, Abu Hanifa's view leaves the wife married; the Sahibayn's view would divorce her.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.
